impassable in wet weather we meet on the road several prussian waggon and reinforcement on they march to bruxelle two of my fellow traveller in the diligence be very intelligent young man belong to respectable family in cologne and be return thither they likewise complain much of the overbearing demeanor of the prussian military towards the burgher cologne be a large but very dull look city as dull as liége it would seem as if all town and city under ecclesiastical domination be dull or render so by the prohibition of the most innocent amusement the fortification be out of repair but the prussian government intend to make cologne a place of great strength the name of the village on the opposite of the river be deutz and in the time of the french occupation there be a _ tête-de-pont _ the next morning i be oblige to appear before the police and afterwards before the _ commandant de la place _ in order to have my passport examine and _ visé _ at the bureau of the police it be remark to I that my passport be not _ en règle _ the feature of the bearer not be therein specify i reply that it be not my fault that it be give to I in that shape by the english consul at bruxelle and that it be not my province to give to the consul any direction as to its form and tenor the commissary of police then ask I what business i be about in travel and the follow conversation take place : be haben sie für geschäfte -- keine ich reise nur um vergnügen 's willen -- sonderbar -- worin liegt da sonderbare dass man reist um ein schönes land zu sehen -lrb- 20 -rrb- -- he make no answer to this but one of he coadjutor stand by he say in a loud whisper ein herumreiser which mean a adventurer or person who travel about for no good -- in a word a suspicious character i then say with the utmost calm and indifference : gentleman as soon as you shall have finish all you commentary on the subject of my passport pray be so good as to inform I what i be to do whether i may go on to mayence and frankfort as be my intention or return to bruxelle the commissary after a slight hesitation sign the _ visa _ and i then carry it to the bureau of the commandant whose secretary sign it without hesitation merely ask I if i be a military man in the afternoon i go to visit the dome or cathedral it be a fine specimen of gothic architecture but singular enough the steeple be not yet finish in this cathedral the most remarkable thing be the chapel of the three king wherein be deposit a massy gold chest inlay with precious stone of all sort and of great value contain the bone of the identical three king -lrb- it be say -rrb- who come from the east to worship the infant jesus at bethlehem the scripture say it be three wise man or magi the legend however call they king and give they gothic name let schoolman and theologian reconcile this difference : _ ce n'est point notre affaire _ to I it appear that when the german tribe embrace christianity and enrol themselves under the banner of st peter it be think but fair to allow they to give vent to a little nationality and to blend they old tradition with the new-fangled doctrine and no doubt the sovereign pontiff think that the people could never be make to believe too much the same policy be practice by the jesuit missionary in china where in order to flatter the national vanity and bend it to they purpose they represent jesus christ as be a great personal friend and correspondent of confucius to return to these monarch wise man or magus : they _ scull _ be keep separate to the rest of the bone and each _ scull _ bear a crown of gold but if you be fond of miracle legend and detail of relic come with I to the church of st ursulum in this city and see the proof positive of the miraculous legend of the eleven thousand virgin who suffer martyrdom in this city in the time of attilum the bone of all of whom be carefully preserve here and adorn the interior wall of the church in the guise of arm arrange in a armoury eleven thousand scull each bear a golden or gilt crown grin horribly on the spectator from the upper part of the interior wall of the church where they be place in a row what a fine subject this would make for a ballad in the style of bürger to suppose that on a particular night in the year at the midnight hour when mortal in slumber be bind the bone all descend from the wall where they be arrange form themselves into body clap on they head and dance a skeleton dance round the ghost of attilum the people of cologne in the time of the ecclesiastical electorate have the reputation of be extremely superstitious and no doubt there be many who implicitly believe this pious tale indeed who could refuse they assent to its authenticity on behold the proof positive in the scull and bone i recollect that in the history of the compère mathiew -lrb- 21 -rrb- the père jean rate mightily the native of cologne for they bigotry and superstition and for the bad reception they give to he and to he philosophy that people be happier from a blind belief as some pretend appear to I extremely problematical for my part under no circumstance can i think bliss to consist in ignorance nor have i feel any particular discomfort in have learn at a very early age to put under my foot as lucretius express it the _ strepitum acheronti avarus _ on the contrary it have make I a perfect cosmopolitan extinguish all absurd national and religious prejudice and render I at home wherever i travel and i meet the catholic the lutheran the moslem the jew the hindou and the guebre as a brother _ quo I cunque ferat tempesta deferor hospe _ -lrb- 22 -rrb- let I add one word more to obviate any misrepresentation of my sentiment from some malignant pharisee that tho ' i be no friend to king-craft and priest-craft and can not endure that religion should ever be blended with politics yet i be a great admirer of the beautiful and consoling philosophy or theosophy of jesus christ which inculcate the equality of mankind and represent the creator of the universe the author of all be as the universal father of the human race cologne derive its name from _ colonia _ as it be a roman colony plant here to protect the left bank of the rhine from the incursion of the german horde it be here that the grand and original manufactory of the far-famed _ eau de cologne _ be to be see the _ eau de cologne _ be a sovereign remedy for all kind of disorder and if the _ affich _ of the proprietor jean-marie farina be worthy of credit he be as formidable a check to old pluto as ever aesculapius be the sale of this water be immense on my return to the inn i meet with a dutch clergyman who be travel with he pupil three very fine boy the son of a dutch lady of rank he be to conduct they to the university of neuwied on the right bank of the rhine in order to place they there for they education the young man seem to have profit much from they study they tutor seem to be a well-informed man and of liberal idea he prefer speak german to french as he say he have not much facility in express himself in the latter language he say if i be go he way he would be happy to have the pleasure of my company to which i very willingly accede and we agree to start the next morning early so as to arrive at bonn to breakfast and then to go on to godesberg where he propose to remain a few day from the window of we inn we have a fine view of the river and i have not omit do hommage to old father rhine by take up some of he water in the hollow of my hand to drink the rhine of later year have be consider the guardian of germany against the hostile incursion of the french and schiller represent this river as a swiss vigilant on he post yet in spite of he vigilance and fidelity unable to prevent he restless neighbor from force he safeguard the follow be the line of schiller where the river speak in a distich : treu wie dem schwfeizer gebührt bewach ` ich germanien grenze aber der gallier hüpft über den duldenden strom in vain my stream i interpose to guard germanium 's realm from foe the nimble gaul my care deride and often leap on t ` other side godesberg 4th July the distance from cologne to bonn be 18 mile and godesberg be three mile further we stop to breakfast at bonn and after breakfast make a promenade thro ' the city bonn be a handsome clean well-built and cheerful look city and the house be good and solid the electoral palace be a superb building but be not occupy and be fall rapidly to decay from the terrace in the garden belong to this palace which impend over the rhine you have a fine view of this noble river this palace be at one time make use of as a barrack by the french and since the secularization of the ecclesiastical electorate it have not be think worth while to embellish or even repair it there be a roman antiquity in this town call the _ altar of victory _ erect on the place st remus but remarkable for nothing but its antiquity it seem to be a common roman altar -lrb- 23 -rrb- the road from bonn to godesberg be three mile in length and thro ' a superb avenue of horse-chesnut tree but before you arrive at godesberg there be on the left side of the road a curious specimen of gothic architecture call _ hochkreutz _ very like waltham cross in appearance but much higher and in better preservation it be erect by some feudal baron to expiate a homicide the castle of godesberg be situate on a eminence and command a fine prospect it be now a mass of rum and the wall only remain it derive its name of godesberg or götzenberg from the circumstance of its have be formerly the site of a temple of minerva build in the time of the roman and thence call götzenberg by the christian _ götze _ in german signify a idol on the plain at the foot of the hill of godesberg and at the distance of a eighth of a mile from the river a shelve cornfield intervene stand three large hotel and a ridotto all striking edifice to the south of these be situate a large wood these hotel be always full of company in the summer and autumn : they come here to drink the mineral water a species of seltzer the spring of which be about a quarter of a mile distant from the hotel the hotel at which we put up bear the name of _ die schöne aussicht _ -lrb- la belle vue -rrb- and well do it deserve the name for it command a fine view of the reach of the river north and south directly on the opposite bank abruptly rise be the superb and magnificent chain of mountain call the _ sieben gebirge _ or seven mountain on the summit of these mountain tower the remains of gothic castle or keep still majestic tho ' in ruin and frown on the plain below they bring to one 's recollection the legend and chronicle of the middle age they bear terrible awe-inspiring name such as drachenfel löwenberg the highest of they be call drachenfel or the rock of dragon and on it stand the burg or chateau of a feudal count or _ raubgraf _ who be the terror of the surrounding country and have give rise to a very interesting romance call _ the knight of the seven mountain _ this feudal tyrant use to commit all sort of depredation and descend into the plain below in order to intercept the convoy of merchandize passing between aix-la-chapelle and frankfort it be to check these abuse and oppression that be institute the famous secret tribunal _ da heimliche gericht _ the various government in germany be then too weak to protect they subject or to punish these depredation this secret tribunal from the summary punishment it inflict the mysterious obscurity in which it be envelop and the impossibility of escape from its pursuit become the terror of all germany they have agent and combination everywhere and exercise such a system of espionage as to give to they proceedings a appearance of supernatural agency a simple accusation be sufficient for they to act upon provide the accuser solemnly swear to the truth of it without reserve and consent to undergo the same punishment as the accuse be subject to in case the accusation should be false till this solemnity be go through no pursuit be institute against the offender there be scarcely ever a instance of a false accusation for it be well know that no power could screen the delator from the exemplary punishment that await he and there be no means of escape from the omniscience and omnipotence of the secret tribunal to return to godesberg it be a most beautiful spot and much agreeable society be here to be meet with the family of distinction of the environ country come here for the purpose of recreation and drink the mineral water we sit down usually sixty to dinner and i observe some very fine woman among they on Sunday there be a ball at the ridotto the promenade in the environs be exceedingly romantic and this place be the favorite resort of many new married couple who come here to pass the honeymoon the scenery of the surrounding country be so picturesque and beautiful as to require the pencil of a ariosto or wieland to do justice to it : ne se tutto cercato avessi il mondo vedria di questo un pin gen til paese -lrb- 24 -rrb- and have he range the universal world would not have see a lovelier in he round -- _ trans _ w rise to the research of the naturalist and mineralogist the seven mountain offer inexhaustible resource the living and accommodation of the three hotel be very reasonable for one and a half florin you have a excellent and plentiful dinner at the table d'hôte include a bottle of moselle wine and seltzer water at discretion by pay extra you can have the rhine wine of different growth and crop and french wine of all sort i be much pleased with the little i have see of the german woman they appear to be extremely well educate i observe many of they in they morning walk with a book in they hand either of poetry or a novel schiller be the favorite poet among they and augustus lafontaine the favorite novel writer -lrb- 25 -rrb- he be a very agreeable author be he not so prolix yet we english have no right to complain of this fault since there be no novel in all germany to compare in point of prolixity with clarissa sit charle grandison or tom jone the great fault of augustus lafontaine be that of include in one novel the history of two or three generation a beautiful and very interesting tale of he however be entirely free from this defect and be found on a fact it be call _ dankbarkeit und liebe _ -lrb- gratitude and love -rrb- there be more real pathos in this novelette than in the _ nouvelle héloïse _ of rousseau ehrenbreitstein 8 July after a _ sèjour _ of three day at godesberg we leave that delightful residence and proceed to neuwy to deposit the boy we stop however for a hour or two at andernach which be situate in a beautiful valley on the left bank we view the remains of the palace of the king of austrasium and the church where the body of the emperor valentinian be preserved embalmed andernach be remarkable for be the exact spot where julius caesar first cross the rhine to make war on the german nation directly opposite neuwied which be on the right bank stand close to the village of weissenthurm the monument erect to the french general hoche we cross over to neuwy in a boat neuwy be a regular well-built town but rather of a sombre melancholy appearance and be only remarkable for its university science could not chuse a more tranquil abode this university have be ameliorate lately by its present sovereign the king of prussium it be not the interest of napoleon to favor any establishment on the right bank at the expence of those on the leave the former be out of he territory at neuwied i take leave of my agreeable fellow traveller as they intend to remain there and i to go on to ehrenbreitstein a opportunity present itself the same afternoon of which i profit i meet with a austrian captain of infantry and he lady at the inn where i stop who be go to ehrenbreitstein in they _ calèche _ and they be so kind as to offer I a place in it i find they both extremely agreeable both be from austrium proper he have leave the austrian service some time ago and have since enter into the russian service from that he be lately transfer together with the battalion to which he belong into the service of prussium and place on the retired list of the latter with a very small pension he do not seem at all satisfy with this arrangement he have serve in several campaign against the french in germany italy and france and be well conversant in french and italian litterature we stop _ en passant _ at a _ maison de plaisance _ and superb english garden belong to the duke of nassau-weilburg the house be in the style of a cottage _ orné _ but very roomy and tastefully fit up but nothing can be more diversified and picturesque than the manner in which the garden be lay out the ground be much broken favor this and in one part of it be a ravine or valley so romantic and savage that you would fancy yourself in tinian or juan fernandez we arrive late in the evening in the thal ehrenbreitstein which lie at the foot of the gigantic hill fortress of that name which frown over it and seem as if it threaten to fall and crush it my friend land I at the inn _ zum weissen pferd _ -lrb- the white horse -rrb- where there be most excellent accommodation just opposite ehrenbreitstein on the left bank be coblentz a superb fly bridge which pass in three minute keep up the communication between the two town early the next morning i ascend the stupendous rock of ehrenbreitstein which have a great resemblance to the hill fort in indium such as gooty nundydroog etc it be a place of immense natural strength but the fortification be destroy by the french who do not chuse to have so formidable a neighbor so close to they frontier as the rhine then be the prussian government however to whom it now belong seem too fully aware of its importance not to reconstruct the fortification with as little delay as possible ehrenbreitstein completely command all the adjacent country and enfilade the embouchure of the moselle which flow into the rhine at coblentz where there be a elegant stone bridge across the moselle troops without intermission continue to pass over the fly bridge bind to france from the different german state viz saxon hessian prussian etc so that one might apply to this scene anna comnena 's expression relative to the crusade and say that all germany be tear up from its foundation and precipitated upon france i suppose no less than 70000 man have pass within these few day the german papers particularly the _ rheinische mercur _ continue to fulminate against france and the war yell resound with as much fury as ever from the number of troops that continue to pass it would seem as if the ally do not mean to content themselves with the abdication of napoleon but will endeavor to dismember france the prussian officer seem to speak very confidently that alsace and lorraine will be sever from france and reunite to the germanic body to which they say every country ought to belong where the german language be speak and they be continually cite the word of a old song : will ist das deutsche vaterland will man die deutsche zunge spricht da ist da deutsche vaterland -lrb- 26 -rrb- in english : where be the country of the german where the german language be speak there be the country of the german coblentz be a clean handsome city but there be nothing very remarkable in it except a fine and spacious place but in the neighborhood stand the _ chartreuse _ situate on a eminence command a fine view of the whole _ thalweg _ this _ chartreuse _ be one english mile distant from the town and my friend the austrian captain have the goodness to conduct I thither it be a fine large building but be fall rapidly to decay be appropriate to no purpose whatever the country be beautiful in the environs of this place and have repeatedly call forth the admiration and delight of all traveller near coblentz be the monument erect to the french general marceau who fall gloriously fight for the cause of liberty respect by friend and foe July 10th we have a large society this day at the table d'hôte the conversation turn on the restoration of the bourbon which nobody at table seem to desire several anecdote be related of the conduct of the bourbon prince and of the emigration who hold they court at coblentz when they first emigrate these anecdote do not redound much to they honor or credit and i remark that they be hold in great disgust and abhorrence by the inhabitant of these town on account of they treacherous and unprincipled conduct it be from here that la cour de coblentz as it be call intrigue by turn with the jacobin and the brissotin and by betray the latter to the former be in part the cause of the sanguinary measure adopt by robespierre -lrb- 27 -rrb- the object of this atrocious policy be that the french people would by witness so many execution become disgusted at the sanguinary tyranny of robespierre and recall the bourbon unconditionally which fortunately for france and thanks to the heroism and bravery of the republican army do not take place for have the restoration take place at that time a dreadful reaction would have be encourage and the cruelty of the reign of terror surpass with the same view emissary be dispatch from the court of coblentz to the south of france in order under the disguise of patriot to preach up the most exaggerated corollary to the theory of liberty and equality among other thing at ehrenbreitstein be a superb pleasure barge belong to the duke of nassau for water excursion up and down the rhine a _ coche d'eau _ start from here daily to mayence and another to cologne the price be ten frank the person the superb _ chaussée on _ the left bank of the rhine which extend all the way from cologne to mayence be construct by the direction of napoleon in the evening i go to the theater at coblentz where mozart 's opera of don giovannus be represent i recollected my old acquaintance la ci darem la mano which i have often hear in england mayence 12th July i embark in the afternoon of the 11th in the _ coche d'eau _ bind to mayence except a old schiffer i be the only passenger on board as few chuse to go up stream on account of the delay i however be master of my own time and wish to view the lovely scenery on the bank of the river prefer this conveyance and i be highly gratify after boppart the bed of the river narrow much high rock on each bank hem in the stream and render it more rapid nothing can be more sublime and magnificent than the scenery at every turn of the river you would suppose its course block up by rock perceive no visible outlet remain of gothic castle be to be see on they summit at a short distance from each other and where the bank be not abrupt and _ escarpés _ there be _ coteaux _ cover with vine down to the water 's edge the toll of the bell at the different village on the bank give a most aweful solemn religious sound and the reverberation be prolong by the high rock which seem to shut you out from the rest of the world there be the wall nearly entire of two castle of the middle age the one call die katze -lrb- the cat -rrb- the other die maus -lrb- the mouse -rrb- each have its tradition for which and for many other interesting particulars i refer you to klebe 's and schreiber 's description of the bank of the rhine we arrive early in the evening at st goar where we stop and sleep st goar be a fine old gothic town romantically situate and be famous from have two whirlpool in its neighborhood it be completely command and protect by rheinfel a ancient hill fortress but the fortification of which no longer exist it require half a hour 's walk to ascend to the summit of rheinfel but the traveller be well repay for the fatigue of the ascent by the fine view enjoy from the top i remain at rheinfel nearly a hour what a solemn stillness seem to pervade this part of the river only interrupted by the occasional splash of the oar and the toll of the steeple bell bingen on the right bank be the next place of interest and on a island in the center of the river face bingen stand the ruin of a celebrated tower call have the maüsethurm -lrb- mouse tower -rrb- so name from the circumstance of bishop hatto have be devour therein by rat accord to the tradition this be represent as a punishment from heaven on the say bishop for he tyranny and oppression towards the poor but the story be invent by the monk in order to vilify he memory for it appear he be obnoxious to they on account of he attempt to enforce a rigid discipline among they and to check they licentiousness bieberich a superb palace belong to the duke of nassau on the right bank next present itself to view on you left ascend to you right at a short distance from bieberich you catch the first view of mayence on the left bank with its tower and steeple rise from the glade we reach mayence at 4 o'clock pm and i go to put up at the three crown -lrb- _ drei-krone _ -rrb- the first news i learn on arrive at mayence be that napoleon have surrender himself to the captain of a english frigate at oléron but though particulars be not give loui xviii be say to be restore which i be very sorry to hear the ally then have be guilty of the most scandalous infraction of they most solemn promise since they declare that they make war on napoleon alone and that they never mean to dictate to the french people the form of government they be to adopt napoleon have surrender and loui be restore the war may be consider as end for the present unless the ally should attempt to wrest any province from france and in this case there be no say what may happen this have finally end the career of napoleon there be in mayence a remarkably fine broad spacious street call die grosse bleiche and in general the building be striking and solid but too much crowd together as be the case in all ancient fortified city the cathedral be well worth see and contain many thing of value and costly relic when one view the thing of value in the church here at aix-la-chapelle and at cologne what a contradiction do it give to the calumny spread against the french republican that they plunder the -rrb- of great strength which be separate from the town by a esplanade the _ place du marché _ be striking and in the _ place verte _ i saw for the first time in my life the austrian uniform there be some good painting in the picture gallery here and this and the fortification be nearly all that need call forth the attention of a traveller who make but a fleeting visit frankfort-on-the-mayn 14th they and a foreigner in the bargain and that therefore this blame of the french army come from the mouth of a englishman surprise he the more so as the duke of marlborough the boast and pride of the good appropriate and the singing very fair the theater itself be dirty and gloomy the german language appear to I to be better adapt to music than either the french or english the number of dactylic termination in the language give to it all the variety that the _ sdrucciolus _ give to the italian as to poetry no language in the world suit itself better to all the vagary and phantasy of the muse since it possess so much natural rythm and allow like the greek the combination of compound word and a redundancy of epithet and it be besides so flexible that it lend itself to all the ancient as well as the modern metre with complete success : indeed it be the only modern language that i know of which do so as for political opinion here the german seem neither to wish nor to care about the restoration of the bourbon but they talk loudly of the necessity of tear alsace and lorraine from france in fact they wish to put it out of the power of the french ever to invade germany again a thing however little to be hope for for the minor and weaker germanic state have always hitherto -lrb- and will probably again at some future day -rrb- invoke the assistance of france against the greater and stronger i observe that the austrian government be not at all popular here and that its bad faith in financial matter be so notorious and have be so severely feel here that a merchant tell I allude to the bankruptcy of the austrian government on two occasion when there be no absolute necessity for the measure that frankfort have suffer more from the bad faith of the austrian government than from all the war contribution levy by the french bruxelle 28th July on arrival at coblentz we hear that napoleon have surrender himself unconditionally to capt maitland of the _ bellerophon _ he never should have humiliate himself so far as to surrender himself to the british ministry he owe to himself to he brave fellow soldier to the french nation whose sovereign he have be not to take such a step but rather die in the field like we richard iii a glorious death which cast a lustre around he memory in spite of the darker shades of he character or if he could not fall in the field he should have die like hannibal rather than commit himself into the hand of a government in which generosity be by no mean a distinguish feature and which on many occasion have show a petty persecute and vindictive spirit and thus i have no hesitation in portray the characteristic of we tory party which unfortunately for the cause of liberty rule with undivided sway over england he will now end he day in captivity for he destination appear to be already fix and st helena be name as the intended residence he will i say be expose to all the taunt and persecution that petty malice can suggest and this with the most uncomfortable reflection : for have he be more considerate of the spirit of the age he might have set all the monarch ultra and oligarch and they minister at defiance but he wish to ape charlemagne and the caesar and to establish a universal empire : a thing totally impossible in we day and much to be deprecate be it possible consign to st helena napoleon will furnish to posterity a proverb like that of dionysius at corinth this banishment to st helena will be very ungenerous and unjust on the part of the english government but i suppose they satellite and adherent will term it a act of clemency and some _ church and kingman _ would no doubt recommend hew he in piece as samuel do to agag i stop three day at aix-la-chapelle to drink the water and then come royal it would become a perfect pandemonium and would require a army to keep the peace the french police keep a very sharp look-out on all political offence but be more indulgent towards all moral one to attack a man of wealth and power but a poor artisan or labourer who buy a piece of meat after twelve o'clock on Saturday night or a glass of spirit during church-time on Sunday be term a museum -lrb- of sculpture and painting -rrb- no it can not be they never surely can be guilty of such a act of vandalism and contemptible spite i be aware that there be a great clamor amongst a certain description of english for restore these statue and picture to the country from whence they come and that it be the fashion to term the translation of they to pari a revolutionary robbery but let we bring these gentleman to a calm reasoning on the subject the statue and painting in question belong either to government at war with france or to individual inhabit those country now with respect to individual i will venture to affirm on the best authority that the property of no individual be take from he without a equivalent those who have statue and picture of value and wish to sell they receive they full value from the french government but there be no force use on the occasion in fact many who be in want of money be rejoice at the opportunity of sell as they could never have otherwise dispose of those valuable article to individual at the same price that the french government give i recollect a day or two ago be in conversation with a milanese on this subject and other connect with the occupation of italy by the french i happen to mention that the conquest of italy by the republican army must have be attend with confiscation of property he assure I that no such thing as confiscation of property take place that so far from be the loser by the french invasion and the establishment of they system they have on the contrary be considerable gainer for that the country flourish under they domination in a manner before unknown and that one of the greatest advantage attendant on the occupation be the establishment of a equality of weight and measure the decimal division of the coin the introduction of a admirable code of law free would from all barbarism -- legal political and theological -- and intelligible to all class so that there be no occasion to cite old author and go back for three or four hundred year to hunt out authority and precedent for what man of sense could determine at once by follow the dictate of they own judgment with respect to the statue and picture belong to the different government of italy it must never be forget that these government make war against the french revolution either openly or insidiously and do they utmost to aid the coalition to crush the infant liberty of france those who do not act openly do so covertly and indirectly in short from they tergiversation and intrigue they have no claim whatever on the mercy of the conqueror who treat they with a great deal of clemency the destruction of these government be loudly call for by the people themselves who look on the french as they deliverer it will be admit i believe that it be and have be the custom on the continent in all war for all party to levy war contribution on the conquer or occupy country but buonoparte think it more glorious for the french name to take work of art instead of money and not a statue or picture be take from the vanquished government except by a solemn treaty of cession or give in lieu of contribution at the option of the owner and the prince be very glad to give up they picture and statue which the most of they do not know how to appreciate in lieu of money which they be all anxious to keep and on these article a fair value be fix by competent judge in this manner do the french become the possessor of these valuable object of art and in this manner be the noble museum in paris fill up and surely nothing could be more generous and liberal than the use make of the museum by the french government foreigner be indeed more favored than the inhabitant themselves to the inhabitant of pari this museum be open twice a week but to foreigner on produce they passport it be open every day in the week all the year round artist of all nation be allow during a certain number of hour each day to come to copy the statue and picture which suit they taste and stove be light for they accommodation during winter and all this grati -- now before these object of art be collect here they be distribute be admit into the government palace be a matter of favor and here also fee be require -lrb- 32 -rrb- here in the louvre there be no introduction require no court to be pay to _ major-domo _ no favor it be open to all class high and low without exception and no money be allow to be give but there be some people in they ridiculous fury against the french revolution who would fain persuade we that before that epoch there be a golden age on the earth that there be no act of violence commit no fraud practice no property injure no individual ill-used that every prince govern like numa that every noble be a bayard and every priest like a primitive apostle why i need go no further than the seven year ' war to show that in that war during the height of european civilisation and carry on between the most polished nation in europe there be much more act of violence and rapine carry on than ever be do by the french republican i by no means wish to excuse or even palliate the act of ferocity which take place at that epoch of the french revolution call the reign of terror which be execute by a people work up to frenzy by a recollection of they wrong and i know too well that many virtuous individual fall victim to they indiscriminating fury but i do believe and aver that much more clamor be make at the execution of a handful of corrupt courtier intriguing and profligate woman of quality and worthless priest than all the rest put together to return to the seven year ' war -lrb- i may be permit to take this retrospect i hope since it be the fashion and those who differ with I in opinion go much farther back than i do -rrb- let the french royalist and emigrant recollect the confiscation of property and barbarity exercise by marshall richelieu in hanover where many family be reduce to beggary they may not chuse to recollect this but the hanoverian do and they have not forget the _ pavillon de hanovre _ so call by the wit of the time from its have be build by the marshall with money arise from the spoil of hanover will they recollect also the harsh treatment inflict on the burgher and citizen of a town in germany who be shut up in a room and keep without food or drink for nearly three day because they would not consent to fix a heavy and unwarrantable contribution on they fellow citizen when these unhappy but virtuous man be only allow to go out for the necessity of nature attend by sentry and on the third day when faint with hunger a little bread and water be give to they with a assurance that in future they be not to expect such luxury have they forget the devastation commit in berlin by the austrian in the seven year ' war when they pillage burn or destroy all the valuable property of the royal palace the most valuable work of art vase statue of antiquity the loss of which could never be replace when they lop off the head arm and leg of the statue have they forget the conduct of the belligerent power at the siege of dresden at the same epoch when whole family among whom be helpless old man and woman with child at the breast be compel to leave dresden in the middle of a most rigorous winter and be drive to take refuge in the field where the most of they perish with hunger and cold and where many individual lose they reason and become insane from the treatment they receive have they forget the merciless barbarity inflict by the russian in the same war on the inhabitant of the prussian territory they rip up and burn man woman and child and the dreadful retaliation inflict on they at the battle of zorndorff when the prussian exasperate at the idea of those horror so fresh in they memory on be order to bury the russian dead throw the wound man also belong to that nation into the grave dig for the dead to be thus bury alive and hastily fill they up with earth as if fearful that they might relent do they give themselves time for reflection these be not exaggeration they be give by a author celebrate for he impartiality and deep research and who be a eye-witness of many of these proceedings i mean archenholz in he admirable history of the seven year ' war -lrb- 33 -rrb- then again in the war of american independence -lrb- and here my countryman must excuse I if i point out the act of injustice commit by they when act in obedience to a unprincipled and arbitrary government and in a cause hostile to freedom -rrb- to destroy or deface and the valuable public library too which be burn what excuse can be offer for this be the time of omar return it be fair and allow by the law of war to blow up and destroy arsenal magazine contain warlike store and engine of destruction but to destroy with gothic barbarity building of great symmetry and beauty and a library too -- o fie why i will defy any man to point out a single instance where the french republican army or napoleon ever injure or wantonly destroy a single national edifice a single work of art a single book belong to any other country on the fall twice into they possession they never destroy or take away a single article but on the contrary there as well as in berlin they invite the inhabitant to form a civic guard for the protection of they property as to the vandalism shewn during the reign of terror and i by no means seek to palliate it that be of short duration it be madness if you will but it be disinterested -- and other nation but surpass perhaps by more dreadful scene commit at wexford in 1798 under the auspices of the government then rule ireland and which the noble and virtuous -- -lrb- 35 -rrb- disdain to serve excuse verse -- the abbé delille -- the opéra comique i meet with my brother-in-law and he nephew at pari and hearing from they that they have a intention of return to england by the way of bruxelle with the idea of visit the plain of waterloo i be induce to accompany they we start on the 18th August take the exact route from pari that be take by napoleon pass the first night at st quentin the second at a and miss o'neil and while they be on the stage i be all eye and ear but the other actor be always so inferior that the contrast be too obvious and it only serve to make more conspicuous the flagging of interest that pervade the tragedy of shakespeare _ macbeth _ alone perhaps excepted i speak only of shakespeare 's fault as a dramaturgus and they be rather the fault of he age than he own for in everything else i think he the greatest litterary genius that the world ever produce and i place he far above any poet ancient or modern yet in allow all this i do not at all wonder that he dramatic piece do not in general please foreigner and that they be disgust with the low buffoonery interruption of interest and want of arrangement that ought of necessity to constitute a drama for i feel the same objection myself when read shakespeare and often lose patience but then when i come to some sublime passage i become wrapt up in it alone and totally forget the piece itself in order to inspire a foreigner with admiration for shakespeare i would not give he he play to read entire but i would present he with a _ recueil _ of the most beautiful passage of that great poet and i be sure he would be so delighted with they that he would readily join in the all hail that the british nation award he thus you may perceive the distinction i make between the creative genius who design and the artist who fill up the canvas between the poet and the dramaturgus i be probably singular in my taste as a englishman when i tell you that i prefer shakespeare for the closet and racine or voltaire or corneille for the stage : and with regard to english tragedy i prefer as a act drama home 's _ dougla _ -lrb- 46 -rrb- to any of shakespeare 's _ macbeth _ alone except and for this plain reason that the interest in _ dougla _ never flag nor be divert in give my mite of admiration to the french stage i be fully aware of its fault of the long declamation and the _ fade galanterie _ that prevail before voltaire make the grand reform in that particular : and on this account i prefer voltaire as a tragedian to racine and corneille the _ phédre _ and _ athalie _ of racine be certainly masterpiece and little inferior to they be _ iphigénie andromaque _ and _ britannicus _ but in the other i think he must be pronounced inferior to voltaire as a proof of my argument i need only cite _ zaïre alzire mahomet sémiramis l'orphelin de la chine brutus _ voltaire have i think unite in he dramatic writings the beauty of corneille racine and crébillon and have avoid they fault this however be not i believe the opinion of the french in general but i follow my own judgment in affair of taste and if anything please I i wait not to ascertain whether the master have say so it show a delicate attention on the part of the director of the _ théâtre français _ now that so many foreigner of all nation be here to cause to be represent every night the masterpiece of the french classical dramatic author since these be piece that every foreigner of education have read and admire and he would much rather go to see act a play with which he be thoroughly acquaint than a new piece of one which he have not read for as the recitation be extremely rapid it would not be so easy for he to seize and follow it without previous reading of molière i have already see the _ avare _ the _ femme savante _ and the _ fourbery de scapin _ since these i have see the _ tartuffe _ and _ george dandin _ both inimitably perform how i enjoy the scene of the _ pauvre homme _ in the _ tartuffe _ and the lecture give to george dandin by m and mme de sotenville wherein they recount the virtue and merit of they respective ancestor of molière indeed there be but one opinion throughout europe in the comic line he bear away the palm unrivalled and here i fully agree with the general i must not quit the subject of french theatricals without speaking of the _ opéra comique _ at the _ théâtre faydeau _ it be to the sort of light piece that be give here that the french music be peculiarly appropriate and it be here that you seize and feel the beauty and melody of the national music these little _ chanson _ _ romance _ and _ arietta _ be so please to the ear that they imprint themselves durably on the memory which be no equivocal proof of they merit i can not say as much for the tragic singing in the _ opéra serium _ at the grand french opera which to my ear sound a perfect psalmody there be but one language in the world for tragic recitative and that be italian on the other hand in the _ genre _ of the _ opéra comique _ the french stage be far superior to the italian in the french comedy everything be graceful and natural the italian can not catch this happy medium so that they comedy and comic national cause and the voice of the people and by no means to become the blind tool of the prince for it be absurd as it be degrade to humanity it be impious to consider the prince as the proprietor military despotism press hard upon the unhappy savoyard and wring from he he hard-earned pittance while no people be better off than the vaudoi yet the savoyard be to the full as deserving of liberty as the swiss the savoyard possess honesty fidelity and industry in a superior degree and these quality he seldom or ever lose even when expose to the temptation of a great metropolis like pari to which they be compel to emigrate as they own country be too poor to furnish the means of subsistence to all its population when in paris and other large city the savoyard contrive by the most indefatigable industry and incredible frugality to return to they native village after a certain lapse of time with a little fortune that be amply sufficient for they comfort the poorest savoyard in paris never fail to remit something for the support of he parent both voltaire and rousseau have render justice to the good quality of this honest people it be a thousand pity that this country -lrb- savoy -rrb- be not either incorporate with france or make to form part of the helvetic confederacy on pass by la meillerie we be remind of la nouvelle héloise and the word of st preux : le rocher est road into italy pass thro ' the whole length of this canton napoleon cause it to be separate from the helvetic union and to form a republic apart with the ulterior view and which he afterwards carry into execution of annex it to the french empire the valai form a long and exceedingly narrow valley thro ' the whole length of which the rhône flow and fall into the lake leman at st gingolph the breadth of this valley in its widest part be not more probably than 1000 yard and in most place considerably narrower and it be enclose on each side or rather wall up by the immense mountain of the higher alp which rise here very abruptly and seem to shut out this valley from the rest of the world the high road run nearly parallel to the course of the rhône and be sometimes on one side of the river and sometimes on the other communicate by bridge from the sinuosity of the road and the different point of view present by the salient and re-enter angle of the mountain the scenery be extremely picturesque grand and striking and as sometimes no outlet present itself to view you do not perceive how you be ever to get out of this valley but by a stratagem similar to that of sindbad in the morning we arrive at sion call in the language of the country sitten the metropolis of the valai it be a neat-looking and tolerably large town and which from its position might be make a most formidable military post as there be a steep hill close to it which rise abruptly from the center of the valley and command a extensive view east and west work erect on this height would enfilade the whole road either way and totally obstruct the approach of a enemy there be besides a large castle on the southern _ parous _ of mountain which hem in this valley which would expose to a most galling fire and take in flank completely those who should attempt to force the passage whether come from st maurice or brieg we stop two hour at sion to mend a wheel and this give I time to ascend the ascertain what be the reason that induce the king to build a church in a foreign territory i do not observe either on the road or in any of the village thro ' which we pass any striking specimen of valaisan female beauty but i often remark the prominent bosom that rousseau describe as frequent among they we meet with several _ crétins _ or idiot all of whom have _ goitre _ in a greater or less independence and neglect of decency and cleanliness democritus as to they disposition to laugh perpetually and aristippus inasmuch as they seem to be perfectly contented with they state they be in general fat and well feed for the poorest inhabitant give they something they have a good deal of cunning and many curious anecdote be related of they which shew that they be endowed with a sort of sagacity resemble the instinct of animal i recollect one myself mention by zimmermann in he essay on solitude of a crétin who be accustom to imitate with he voice the sound of the village clock whenever it strike the hour and quarter one day by some accident the clock stop yet the cretin go through the chime of the hour and quarter with the same regularity as the clock would have do have it be go we arrive at night at the village of brieg at the foot of the simplon and put up at a very comfortable inn brieg and glisse be two small village lie within a quarter of a mile distance from each it make on my mind on arrival at the village of the simplon which lie at nearly the greatest elevation off the road and be more than half-way across i write in my enthusiasm for the author of this tuoi miracoli vincesti napoleon ' più grandus ostacolus imagine a fine road or causeway broad enough for three carriage to go abreast cut in the flank of the mountain wind along they contour sometimes but in speaking of theatrical performance no person should leave milan without go to see the _ teatro girolamo _ which be one of the curiosity of the place peculiar to milan and more frequented perhaps than any other this be a puppet theater but puppet so well contrived and so well work as to make the spectacle well worth the attention of the traveller it be the _ nec plus ultra of marionettism _ in which signer girolamo the proprietor have make a revolution which will form a epoch in the annals of puppetry have drive from the stage entirely the _ graziosissima maschera d'arlecchino _ who use to be the hero of all the piece represent by the puppet and substitute himself or rather a puppet bear he name in the place of harlequin as the principal _ farceur _ of the performance he have contrived to make the puppet girolamo a little like himself but so much caricatured and so monstrously ugly a likeness that the bare sight of it raise immediate laughter the theater itself be small be something under the size of we old haymarket little theater but be very neatly and tastefully fit up the puppet be about half of the natural size of man and girolamo aid by one or two other work they and give they gesture by means of string which be however so well contrived as to be scarcely visible and girolamo himself speak for all as besides be a ventriloquist he have a most astonishing faculty of vary he voice and adapt it to the _ rôle _ of each puppet so that the illusion be complete the scenery and decoration be excellent sometimes he give opera as well as drama and there be always a _ ballo _ with transformation of one figure into another which form part of the performance these transformation be really very curious and extremely well execute almost all the piece act on the theater be of girolamo 's own composition and he sometimes choose a classical or mythological subject in which the puppet girolamo be sure to be introduce and charge with all the wit of the piece he speak invariably with the accent and _ patois _ of the country and he joke never fail to keep the audience in a roar of laughter he mode of speech and slang phrase form a absurd contrast to the other figure who speak in pure italian and pompous _ versus scioltus _ for instance the piece i see represent be the story of alcesti and be entitle _ la scesa d'ercole nell inferno _ to redeem the wife of admetus hercule before he commence this undertaking wish to hire a valet for the journey have a interview with girolamo and engage he hercule speak in blank verse and in a phrase full of _ sesquipedalium verba _ demand he country and lineage girolamo reply in the piedmontese dialect and with a strong nasal accent : _ de mi pais de piemong _ girolamo however though he profess to be as brave as mar himself have a great repugnance to accompany he master to the shades below or to the _ casa del diavolo _ as he call it and while hercule fight with cerberus he shake and tremble all over as he do likewise when he meet _ madonna morte _ all this be very absurd and ridiculous but it be impossible not to laugh and be amuse at it a anecdote be related of the _ flesh and blood _ girolamo that he have a very pretty wife who take it into she head one day to elope with a french officer and that to revenge himself he dramatize the event and produce it on he own theater under the title of _ colombina scampa coll ` uffiziale _ have fill the piece with severe satire and sarcastic remark against woman in general and colombina in particular the atelier of the famous artist in mosaic rafaellus be well worth inspect and here i have a opportunity of behold a copy in mosaic and nearly finish of the celebrated picture of leonardo da vincus represent the _ caena dominus _ what a useful as well as admirable art be the mosaic to perpetuate the painting of the greatest master i recollect on behold this work that eustace in he _ tour thro ' italy _ -lrb- 55 -rrb- relate with a pious horror that the french soldier use the original picture as a target to practice at with ball cartridge and that christ 's head be single out as the mark this absurd tale which have not the least shadow of truth in it have it appear gain some credit among weak-minded people and i therefore beg leave to contradict it in the most formal manner it be buonaparte who the moment the picture be discover order it to be put in mosaic no the french be the protector and encourager and by no mean the destroyer of the work of art and this ridiculous story of the picture be use as a target be probably invent by the priesthood who seem to have take great delight in impose on poor eustace 's credulity to I it seem that such a story could only have be invent by a monk and believe and repeat by a old woman or a bigot the priest and french emigrant have invent and spread the most shameful and improbable calumny against the french republican and against napoleon and that credulous gull john bull have be silly enough to give full credence to all these tale and stand stare with he eye and mouth open at the recital while a vulgar jobbing ministry -lrb- as cobbet would say -rrb- _ pick he pocket _ quite of a piece with this be the say mr eustace 's bigotry in not chus to call lombardy by its usual appellation lombardy and affectedly term it the plain of the po why so will be ask why because mr eustace hate the ancient lombard and hold they very nearly in as much horror as he do the modern french because as he say they be the enemy of the church and make war on and despoil the holy see the fact be that the lombard prince be the most enlighten of all the monarch of they time they be the first who begin to resist the encroachment of the clergy and to shake off that abject submission to the holy see which be the characteristic of the age the lombard be a fine gallant race of man and not so bigoted as the other nation of europe where have there ever reign a better and more enlighten and more just and humane prince than theodoric -lrb- 56 -rrb- but theodoric be a arian hence mr eustace 's aversion for he with the most servile devotion reject condemn and anathematize whatever the church reject condemn and anathematize for myself i look on the extinction of the lombard power by charlemagne to have be a great calamity have it last the reformation and deliverance of europe from papal and ecclesiastical tyranny would have happen probably three hundred year sooner and the inquisition never have be plant in spain i have make this digression from a love of justice and from a wish to vindicate the french republic and napoleon from one at least of the many unjust aspersion cast on they i feel it also my duty to state on every occasion that i belong to a army send to egypt in order to expel they from that country have be a eyewitness of the good and beneficial reform and improvement that the french make in egypt during a period of only three year they do more for the good of that country in this short period than we have do for indium in fifty year be oblige to be in london on the 24th December i take leave of the agreeable city of milan with much regret on the 19th of October and engage a place in a swiss _ voiture _ go to lausanne my fellow traveller be two brunswick officer in the service of the princess of wale who be return to they native country and a hungarian and he son settle in domo d'ossolum nothing occur till we arrive at arona where we be detain a whole day in consequence of some informality in the passport of the two german viz that of its not have be _ visé _ by the sardinian chargé d'affaire at milan during we detention at arona i fall in with a young frenchman who be go to milan in company of some swiss friend the swiss be permit to proceed but the other be not for no other reason than because he be a frenchman so that he take a place in we carriage in order to return to switzerland i find he a very agreeable companion for tho ' much chagrined and vex at this harsh and ungenerous treatment on the part of the piedmontese authority he soon recover he good humor and contribute much to the pleasure of we journey the german come back to arona very late at night and during the rest of the journey give vent to they feeling with many a execration such as _ verfluchter spitzbube hundsfott _ on the head of the inexorable police officer of arona the next day on pass by belgirate we take a boat to visit the borromean island and afterwards return to rejoin we carriage at fariolo the first of these island that we visit be the _ isolum bellum _ where there be a large and splendid villa belong to the borromean family the room be of excellent and solid structure and there be some good family picture the furniture be ancient but costly the _ rez de chaussée _ or lower part of the house which be completely _ à fleur d'eau _ with the lake be tastefully pave and the wall decorate with a mosaic of shell one would imagine it the abode of a sea nymph i thought of calypso and galatea there be in these apartment _ à fleur d'eau _ two or three exquisite statue lausanne 11th November i have be now nearly three week at lausanne and be much pleased both with the inhabitant who be extremely affable and well-informed and with the beautiful site that environ this city the capital of the canton de vaud the sentiment of the vaudoi with the exception of a few absurd family among the _ noblesse _ who from ignorance or prejudice be stickler for the old time be highly liberal and as they acquire they freedom and emancipate themselves from the yoke of the bernoi thro ' the means of the french revolution they be grateful to that nation and receive with hospitality those who be proscribe by the present french government they behavior thus form a noble contrast to the servility of the genevese the government of the canton de vaud be wholly democratic and be compose of a landamman and grand and petty council all _ bourgeois _ or of the most intelligent among the agricultural class who know the interest of they country right well and be not likely to betray they as the _ noblesse _ be but too often induce to do for the sake of some foolish ribband rank or title the _ noblesse _ be in a manner self-exiled -lrb- so they say -rrb- from all participation in the legislative and executive power for they have too much _ morgue _ to endure to share the government with those whom they regard as _ roturier _ but the real state of the case be that the people will not elect they and the people be perfectly in the right for at the glorious epoch when without bloodsh the burgher and plebeian upset the despotism of bern the conduct of the _ noblesse _ be very equivocal la harpe be the leader of this beneficial revolution for which however the public mind be fully prepared and disposed and la harpe be a virtuous ardent and incorruptible patriot this canton have be for a long period of year in a state of vassalage to that of bern all the post and office of government be fill by bernoi and the vaudoi be exclude from all share in the government and from all public employment of consequence when the sun of revolution after gloriously rise in america have shine in splendor on france and have successfully dissipate the mist of tyranny feudality priestcraft and prejudice it be natural that those state which have languish for so many year in a humiliating situation should begin to look about they and enquire into the origin of all the shackle and restraint impose on they and no doubt the vaudoi soon discover that it be a anomaly in politics as well as in reason that two state of such different origin the one be a latin and the other a teutonic people with language custom and manners so different should be blended together in a system in which all the advantage be on the side of bern and nought but vassalage on the part of vaud a chief be alone want to give the impulse he be soon find the business be settle in forty-eight hour and by the mediation of the french government vaud be declare and acknowledge a independent state and for ever release from the dominion of bern the federative constitution be then abolish throughout the union and a general government call the helvetic republic substitute in its place but this constitution not suit the genius and habit of the people nor the locality of the country be not of long duration trouble break out and insurrection which be foment and encourage by the adherent of the old régime but napoleon by a wise and salutary mediation step in between they and prevent the effusion of blood by restore the old confederation modify by a variety of amelioration in the act of mediation napoleon contented himself with separate the valai entirely from the confederation and shortly after annex it to france on account of the high road into italy across the simplon run thro ' that territory and which it become of the utmost importance to he to be master of the new helvetic confederation be inviolably respect and protect by napoleon for never after the act of mediation do any french troops enter in the canton de vaud or any part of the union to pass into italy they always move on the savoy side of the lake to enter into the valai this act of mediation save probably a good deal of bloodshed and in a very short time give such general satisfaction and be in every respect so useful and beneficial to the helvetic union that in spite of the intrigue of the senate of bern who have never be able to digest the loss of vaud the ally power in the year 1814 solemnly guarantee the helvetic confederation as establish by the act of mediation merely restore the valai to its independence and aggregate it as a independent canton to the general union geneva on its be sever from the french empire and recover its independence solicit the helvetic union to be admit as a member and component part of that confederacy which be agree to and it be and remain aggregated to it also in 1815 on the return of napoleon from elba and on the renewal of the war the bern government make a most barefaced attempt to regain possession of the canton de vaud to this they be no doubt secretly encourage by the ally and principally it be say by the british government the most dangerous artful and determine enemy of all liberty but this project be completely foiled by the penetration energy and firmness of the inhabitant of the canton de vaud and of its government in particular the central government of the union be at that time hold at bern and it be agree upon in the diet that switzerland should remain perfectly neutral during the approach conflict a army of observation of 80000 man be vote and levy to enforce this neutrality but the command of it be give to de watteville who have be a colonel in the english service and be a determine enemy of the french revolution and of everything connect with or arise that this army be disband the directoral canton -lrb- bern -rrb- cause to be intimate to the canton de valid that it be the wish and intention of the high ally to replace switzerland in the exact countryman who should aid or abet this scheme or deliver up a single document to the commissioner traitor and rebel they likewise call on the whole canton to arm in defense of its independence and scorpion to do for augustus : ipse tibus jam brachium contrahit arden scorpio et coeli jusiâ plus part reliquit -lrb- 59 -rrb- i meet with a adventure in my journey from st quentin to compiègne which have it happen a hundred year ago in france would have alarm I much for my personal safety it be as follow i have take my place at st quentin to go to pari but all the diligence be fill the _ bureau _ expedite a _ calèche _ to convey I as far as compiègne there to meet the pari diligence at nine the next morning it be a very dark cold night and snow very hard between eleven and twelve o'clock at night half way between st quentin and compiègne the axle tree of the carriage break we be at least two mile from any village one way and three the other but a lone house be close to the spot where the accident happen we have therefore the choice of go forward or backward the postillion and myself help the carriage on with we hand or to take refuge at the lone house till dawn of day i prefer the latter we knock several time at the door of the lone house but the owner refuse to admit we say that he be sure we be _ gen de mauvaise vie _ and that he would shoot we if we do not go away the postillion and i then determine on retrograde two mile the distance of the nearest village and remain there till morning we arrive there with no small difficulty and labor for it snow very fast and heavily and it require a good deal of bodily exertion to push on the carriage arrive at the village we knock at the door of a small cottage the owner of which sell some brandy he receive I very civilly give I some egg and bacon for supper and a very fair bed the next morning after have the axle tree repair we proceed on we journey to compiègne i suffer much from the cold during this adventure and do not sleep well have fall into a train of thought which prevent I from so do and i could not help bring to my recollection the adventure of raymond in the forest near strassburg in the romance of _ the monk _ nothing worthy of note occur during the rest of the journey but this adventure oblige I to remain one day at compiègne to wait for the next diligence pari April 8th 1816 i deliver my letter to the wardle family and be very much pleased with they i meet a very agreeable society at they house col wardle be quite a republican and very rigid in he principle -lrb- 60 -rrb- he daughter be a young lady of first rate talent and have already distinguish herself by some poetical composition i meet at they house mr walli the sister of sir r wilson -lrb- 61 -rrb- she be a joint march on the left bank of the nile to rosetta i know that there be not a syllable of truth in the story mr walli however tell I that she brother have express deep regret that he ever give be the fashionable game refreshment be hand round and at twelve o'clock the company break up mme fournier be a lady of very distinguish talent and always act a principal rôle herself in the dramatic they and the evening be fill up with music or _ petit jeux _ i meet with several agreeable and distinguished people at this house among whom be m angla mme duthon from the canton de vaud a lady of great vivacity and talent and general guilleminot and he lady col paulet who marry m vanderberg 's second daughter be on the staff of general guilleminot at the battle of waterloo and suffer much from a fever and ague that he catch on the night bivouac i have attend a séance of the institution of the _ sourds-muet _ found by the famous abbé de l'epée and continue with equal success by he successor the abbé s -lrb- icard -rrb- -lrb- 63 -rrb- who deliver the lecture and exhibit the talent and proficiency of he pupil the eldest pupil massieu himself deaf and dumb be a extraordinary genius and he may be say in some measure to direct all the other massieu who have a very interesting and even handsome countenance and manners extremely prepossessing conduct the examination of the pupil by means of sign and write on a slate or paper and it be wonderful to observe the progress make by these interesting young person who have be so harshly treat by nature the definition they give of substance and quality be so just and happy and in they situation definition be everything for they can not learn by rote as other boy often do who in the study of philology acquire only word and not thing or meaning the deaf and dumb person on the contrary acquire at once by this method of instruction the philosophy of grammar and then it be far from be the dry study that many people suppose a german princess who be present exclaim in a transport of admiration at some of the specimen of definition and inference give by the pupil oh i wish that i be bear deaf and dumb be it only to learn grammar properly sir sidney smith be present at this lecture and seem incline to make himself a little too conspicuous for instance before the examination begin he seat himself close by the abbé s -lrb- icard -rrb- and pull a paper out of he pocket say that he have find it on the ground on he way hither and that it be part of a leaf from a edition of cicero which contain a sentence so applicable to the character and talent of he friend the abbé that he request permission to read it aloud and translate it into french for the benefit of those who do not understand latin he then read the sentence the sense to say nothing and the examination begin paris may 5th i form a party with some friend to visit the cemetery of père la chaise we remark in particular the place where poor labédoyère and marshal but it would require a volume to describe to you in detail this interesting cemetery i think the practice of strew flower over the grave be very touching and classic it remind I of the description of marcellus 's death in virgil : manibus date lilium pleni we however strew over the tomb of labédoyère and ney not lily but violet for my friend mr w -lrb- alli -rrb- who be of we party have a great if they once do so woe to the _ chambre introuvable _ as the present chamber of deputy be call certainly such a set of venal merciless and ignorant bigot and blockhead never be collect in any assembly there have occur several scandalous scene at nîmes and other place the protestant be openly insult and threaten and the government be either too weak to prevent it or as be suppose secretly encourage those excess in fact in pari there be two police the one that of the government the other and by far the most troublesome that of _ monsieur _ -lrb- 65 -rrb- and the violent ultra party or as they be and all this be do with the idea of work on fanatical mind to induce they to commit act of outrage and violence on those whom the priest designate as enemy to the faith and on weak one with the idea of frightening they into restore the land and property which they have purchase or inherit and which formerly belong to emigrant or to the church a lady of my acquaintance -lrb- to give you a idea of the art of these holy hypocrite -rrb- send for a priest to confess and to receive absolution not from any faith in the efficacy of the business but merely from a desire of conform to the ceremony of the national worship the priest arrive but begin by apologize to she that he be sorry he could not administer to she the sacrament of absolution she surprize ask the reason he answer that it be because she uncle have purchase church land which she inherit and that unless she could resolve to restore they to the church he could not think of give she absolution the lady be at a loss whether to be indignant at he impudence or to laugh outright at he folly she however assume a become gravity and _ sang-froid _ and tell he that he be very much mistaken if he think he have get hold of a simpleton or a bigot in she that she have send for he merely with the idea of conform to the national worship and not with the most remote persuasion of the necessity or efficacy of he or any other priest 's absolution she add : you conduct have open my eye as to the view of all you cloth i see you be incurable i shall never send for any of you again and be assure this anecdote shall not be forget you may retire the priest abashed and mortified in find himself mistaken in he suppose prey stammer a excuse and retire i intend to remain at pari until after the marriage ceremony of the duke and duchess of berrus and i shall then proceed to lausanne it be expect there will be some disturbance on the occasion of this marriage i have witness a execution by the guillotine on the place de grève near the _ hôtel de ville _ the criminal be guilty of a burglary and murder it be the only execution -lrb- except political one -rrb- that have take place at paris for the last six month whereas in england they be string up by dozen every fortnight independent of there be far less crime commit in france than in england the french code punish but few offence with death why be not the sanguinary english criminal code with death in every line -- why be it not reform i say ` twould be well if we legislator instead of they puerile and frothy declamation against revolutionary principle and the ambition of napoleon would occupy themselves seriously with this subject but then the lawyer would all oppose the simplification of we code they find by experience that a complicated one obstruct by custom statute and act of parliament difficult to be correctly interpret and frequently at variance with each other be a much more profitable thing a much wider and more lucrative field for the exercise of they profession than the simplicity of the code napoléon and they would die of rage and despair at the thought of anybody not a lawyer be able to interpret the law himself now as we country gentleman and member of parliament be always much inclined to take lawyer 's advice and be besides fully persuade and convince that there be no abuse whatever in england and that everything be as it should be there be no hope of any amelioration in this particular all reasoning and argument be lose on such political optimist the punishment of the guillotine certainly appear to be the most humane mode of terminate the existence of a man that could possibly be invent the apparatus be preserve in the _ hôtel de ville _ and be never expose to view or erect on the place of execution till about a hour before the execution itself take place at the hour appoint the criminal be bring to the scaffold fasten to the board place at right angle with the fatal instrument the head protrude thro ' the groove which embrace the neck the executioner pull a cord the axe descend and the head of the criminal fall into a basket the whole ceremony of the execution do not take three minute when the criminal once arrive at the foot of the guillotine there be none of that horrible struggle that take place in the operation of hang June 21st 1816 the ceremony of the marriage of the duke and duchess of berrus pass off quietly enough several people it be true be arrest for seditious expression but no tumult occur a great apprehension seem to prevail lest something should occur but the
