at pompeius -- ed -lrb- 97 -rrb- horace _ carm _ ii 1 7 -- ed -lrb- 98 -rrb- virgil _ aen _ vi 264 -- ed -lrb- 99 -rrb- virgil _ aen _ vi 129 -- ed chapter xii november-december 1816 from rome to florence -- sismondi the historian -- reminiscence of indium -- lucca -- princess elisa baciocchus -- pisa -- the campo santo -- leghorn -- hebrew in leghorn -- lord dillon -- the story of a lose glove -- from florence to lausanne by milan turin and across mont ceni -- lombardy in winter -- the hospice of mont ceni florence novr 20th i bade adieu to rome on the 28th October and return here by the same road i go viz by radicofanus and sienna i arrive here after a journey of six day have be detain one day at aquapendente on account of the swell of the water the day after my arrival here i despatched a letter to pescium to mr sismondi de ' sismondi the celebrated author of the history of the italian republic to inform he of my intended visit to he and i forward to he at the same time two letter of introduction one from colonel wardle and the other from mr piton banker at geneva who mention I in he letter to sismondus as have _ des idées parfaitement analog aux siennes _ i receive a most friendly answer invite I to come to pescium and to pass a few day with he at he villa pescium be thirty mile distant from florence and the same from leghorn i be delighted with the opportunity of see a man whom i esteemed so much as a author and as a citizen and of visit at the same time the different city of tuscany particularly lucca and pisa i accordingly hire a cabriolet and on the morning of the 6th novr drive to prato a good-sized handsome town solidly build ten mile distant from florence the country on each side of the road appear highly cultivate and the road be line with villa and farm house with garden nearly the whole way change horse at prato i proceed ten mile further to pistoia a large elegant and well-built town on the bank of the ombrone the street in pistoium be broad and well paved and the _ palazzo pubblico _ be a striking building so be the _ seminario _ or college here i change horse again and proceed to pescia where i alight at the villa of m sismondus the distance between pistoium and pescium be about ten or eleven mile pescium be a beautiful little town very clean and solidly build lie in a valley surround nearly on all side by mountain its situation be extremely romantic and picturesque and there be several handsome villa on the slope and summit of these mountain on market day pescium be crowd with the country people who flock hither from all part and one be astonish to see such a number of beautiful and well dress country girl industry and comfort be prevalent here as be the case indeed all over tuscany i mean agricultural industry for commerce be just now at a stand i pass three most delightful day and which will live for ever in my recollection with mr sismondus in whom i find a inexhaustible fund of talent and information combine with such a unassuming simplicity of character and manner that he appear to I by far the most agreeable litterary man that i ever meet with he mother who be a lady of great talent and perfectly conversant in english litterature reside with he he sister also be settle at pescium be marry to a tuscan gentleman of the name of fortus the sister have a full share of the talent and amiable quality of she mother and brother with a family of such resource as this you may suppose we conversation do not flag for a moment nor do i recollect in the course of my whole life have pass such a pleasant time and i only wish that the three day could be prolong to three year politics the occurrence of the day live character classical reminiscence french english italian and german litterature afford we a inexhaustible variety of topic for conversation : and the profound local knowledge that mr sismondus possess of italy of its history and antiquity render he communication of the utmost value to the traveller we supper be prolong to a late hour and i question if the supper and conversation of scipio and atticus those _ node caenaeque deum _ -lrb- 100 -rrb- be more piquant or afford more variety than ours shakespeare schiller voltaire ariosto dante filangierus michel angelo washington napoleon all furnished anecdote and reflexion in abundance the last evening that i pass here two family of pescium come in one of the gentleman be a great reader of voyage and travels and indium suddenly become the subject of discourse as i have pass six year in that country during which time i have visit the three presidency of calcutta madra and bombay have ascend the gange as far as benare have visit the mysore country and nizam 's territory have sojourn three week among the splendid and magnificent ruin of bijanagur or bisnagar have travel thro ' the whole of the deccan from pondicherry to cape comorin besides have traverse on horseback the whole circumference of ceylon and across the whole island from east to west by the wanny i be enable to furnish they with many a anecdote from the eastern world which to they be a great treat and i dare say at time my narration appear almost as marvellous as a story in the arabian night particularly when i related the various religious ceremony the grim idol of juggernaut the swing to _ recover cast _ the exposure of old people to the holy death in the gange by stop up they nose mouth and ear with mud and place they on the water 's edge at low tide in order that they should be sweep off at the high water the holy city of benare the magnificent remains of bisnagar the splendid pagoda of ramisseram the policy of the bramin the appalling voluntary penance of the _ jogui _ or _ fakir _ as the european call they the bed of spike the arm hold up in the air for fifteen year the tiger hunt the method of catch the elephant in ceylon the pearl fishery sepoy establishment in short i must have appear to they a ulyss or a sindbad and i dare say that they think i add from time to time a little embellishment from my imagination tho ' i can safely and solemnly aver that i do not extenuate nor exaggerate any thing but simply related what i have myself see and witness mr sismondus be under a sort of banishment from he native country geneva in consequence of the side of the question he take in he writings on the return of the emperor napoleon from elba it be indeed natural for the restore government -lrb- the bourbon -rrb- to desire the removal from france of a man of talent who have expose they past and might scrutinize they future conduct and wilful fault but why the government of geneva should espouse they quarrel and visit one of they most estimable citizen with banishment for opinion not at all connect with nor influential upon geneva appear to I not only absurd and anomalous but unjust in the highest degree but such be the state of degradation to which europe be reduce by the triumph of the old _ régime _ and the swiss government be compel to become the instrument of the vengeance of the coalition but i shall dwell no more on this subject at present let we hope that in a short time a more liberal spirit will arise and the genevese will be eager to recall in triumph the illustrious citizen of whom they have so much reason to be proud we spend we morning mr sismondus and i in promenade towards the most striking point of the country immediately environ pescium and as i have at this time some idea of come to settle in tuscany he be so kind as to conduct I to look at several villa that be to let and i inspect three very beautiful one well furnished and each capable of hold a large family that be to be let for 18 20 and 24 _ loui d'or _ per annum wine and every article of life be of prodigious cheapness here and the inhabitant be so respectable and there be such a absence of all crime that pescia must be a very desirable and economical residence for any foreign family possess a sufficient knowledge of italian to mix with the society of the native there be several ancient and noble family in the neighborhood highly respectable in point of moral character and manners but rather in _ décadence _ in point of fortune it be with the greatest regret that i bade adieu to the amiable sismondus he mother and sister but i hope for a time only as i have some idea of remove my domicile from lausanne to this part of the world i start at 10 o'clock be on the 11th of November and after two hour ' journey in a cabriolet arrive at lucca a distance of ten mile and put up at the _ hôtel del pelicano _ the road run thro ' a highly cultivate country lucca be a large fortified city situate hi a beautifully luxuriant plain or basin surround on all side by hill and mountain of various slope contour and height and abound in villa vineyard mulberry and olive plantation every spot of ground be in cultivation and the industry of the inhabitant of lucca be proverbial indeed the whole territory of this little _ ci-devant _ republic be a perfect paradise the city itself from the massiveness and solidity of the edifice have more of a solemn than a lively appearance but there be a delightful walk on the rampart which be line with tree the street be well pave the extreme antiquity of the city and style of its edifice make it appear less _ rianus _ than the other city in tuscany the cathedral be gothic and there be in it the statue of the four evangelist this and the _ palazzo pubblico _ be the most conspicuous edifice tho ' the republic be annihilate the word _ liberta _ still remain on a escutcheon on the gate of the city lucca tho ' no longer a republic and enclavée in tuscany be for the present a independent state and belong to a infanta of spain -lrb- formerly princess of parma -rrb- who take the title of duchess of lucca it be generally suppose however that on the demise of marium louisa ex-empress of the french and now duchess of parma this family viz the duchess of lucca and she son will resume they ancient possession in the parmesan and that lucca will then be incorporate with tuscany before the fall of napoleon the princess elisa baciocchus he sister be sovereign of lucca and she it be who have embellish the outside of the city with some beautiful promenade she devote she whole time talent and resource to the good of she subject and be highly esteem and much regret by they the present duchess of lucca have no other character but that which seem common to the royal family of france spain and naple viz of be very weak and priest-ridden lucca furnish excellent female servant who be remarkable for they industry and probity they only solace be they lover or _ amoroso _ as they term he and when they enter into the service of any family they always stipulate for one day in the week on which they must have liberty to visit they _ amoroso _ or the _ amoroso _ must be allow to come to the house to visit they this be a ancient custom among they and have no pernicious consequence nor do it interfere with they other good quality at the back of lucca be a immense mountain which stand between it and pisa and intercept the reciprocal view of the two city which be only ten mile distant from each other this mountain and its peculiarity be the very one mention by dante in he _ inferno _ in the _ episode _ of ugolino : _ cacciando il lupo e i lupicini _ al monte per che i pisan veder lucca non ponno -lrb- 101 -rrb- i start from lucca in a cabriolet and in two hour arrive at pisa put up at the _ tre donzelle _ on the quaus of the arno between lucca and pisa be the _ bagnus di lucca _ a favorite resort for the purpose of bathing and drink the mineral water pisa be one of the most beautiful city i have see in italy the extreme elegance and comfort of the house the spacious quaus on the arno which furnish a most agreeable promenade the splendid style of architecture of the _ palazzo _ and public building the cleanliness of the street the salubrity of the climate the mildness of the winter the profusion and cheapness of all the necessaries of life and above all the amenity and simplicity of the inhabitant combine to make pisa a agreeable and favorite residence yet the population have much decrease there appear a air of melancholy stillness about the city and grass may be see in some of the street this decay in population cause lodgings to be very cheap the most striking object in pisa be the lean tower _ -lrb- torre cadente -rrb- _ and after that the cathedral baptistery and _ campo santo _ which be all close to the tower and to each other imagine two fine gothic church in a square or place like lincoln 's inn field a large oblong building nearly at right angle with the church and inclose a green grass plot in its quadrangle and a lean tower of cylindrical form face the church : and then you will have a complete idea of this part of pisa i must not omit to mention that there be a breed of camel here belong to the grand duke i believe it be the only part of europe except turkey where the breed of camel be attempt to be propagate leghorn 17 novr i leave pisa for leghorn on the morning of the 15th November and after a drive of two hour in a cabriolet i arrive at the latter place and put up at the _ aquilum nera _ the distance between pisa and leghorn be only 10 or 11 mile and a plain with few tree either plant in corn or in pasturage form the landscape between the two city leghorn -lrb- livorno -rrb- be a modern city do not offer anything remarkably interesting to the classical traveller either from its locality or its history found under the auspices of the medicus it have rise rapidly to grandeur and opulence and have eclipse genoa in commerce it be a remarkably handsome city the street be all broad and at right angle the _ piazze _ be large and the _ piazza grande _ in particular be magnificent there be a fine broad street lead from the _ piazza grande _ to the port the port and mole be striking object and considerable commercial bustle prevail there among the few thing worthy of particular notice be the jewish synagogue decorate with costly lamp and inscription in gold in the hebrew and spanish language many of which allude to the hospitality and protection afford to the hebrew nation by the sovereign of tuscany there be a great number of hebrew family here : they all speak spanish be the descendant of those unfortunate jew who be expel from spain at the time of the expulsion of the moor in the reign of don felipe iii surname _ el discreto _ who be determine not to suffer either a jew mahometan or heretic in all he dominion this barbarous decree be the ruin and destruction of a number of industrious family thousand of whom die of despair at be exile from they native land in return for this what have spain gain the inquisition -- despotism in its worst form -- poverty -- rag -- louse -- a overbearing insolent and sanguinary priesthood of whom the monarch be either the puppet or the slave a degraded nobility a half savage grossly ignorant lazy and brutal people a proper judgment on the spanish nation for its cruelty and fanaticism my guide at leghorn conduct I to see the bury ground belong to the english factory which be interesting enough from the variety of tomb monument and inscription here all protestant to whatever nation they belong be bury i notice smollett 's tomb it be on the whole a interesting spot tho ' not quite so much so as the cemetery of père la chaise at paris i return to florence from leghorn _ tout d'une traite _ in the diligence we stop at fornacettus -lrb- half way -rrb- to dine there be a good _ table d'hôte -lrb- ordinario -rrb- _ there florence 22nd novr i have become acquaint with lord dillon -lrb- 102 -rrb- and he family who be reside here and from whom i have receive much civility i meet at he house the marchese giulianus one of the adherent of king joachim a very amiable and clever man who speak english fluently lord dillon be a man of much reading and information and he conversation be at all time a great treat he lady too be very amiable and accomplished i go one day with a friend of mine to a _ pique-nique _ party at the cascino where a laughable adventure occur perfectly in the stile of the _ novella _ of boccacio as it be not the custom in florence that husband and wife should go together to place of public amusement the lady be generally accompany by she _ cavalier servente : _ but it by no means follow that the _ cavalier servente _ be the favored lover : one be often adopt as a cover to another who enjoy the peculiar favor of the lady a gentleman who arrive at the hall where the supper table be lay out somewhat earlier than the rest of the company and before the chamber be light observe a gentleman and lady ascend the staircase turn aside by a corridor and enter a chamber together it be dark and he could not distinguish they person he wait fifteen or twenty minute and observe they leave the chamber together pass along the corridor and disappear he have the curiosity to go into the chamber they have just leave and find on the bed a lady 's glove he take up the glove and put it in he pocket determine that this incident should afford he some amusement at supper and the company also by put some fair one to the blush accordingly when the supper be nearly over he hold up the glove and ask with a loud voice if any lady have lose a glove when he own wife who be sit at the same table at some distance from he call out with the utmost _ sangfroid : e il mio dammelo : l'ho lasciato cadere _ you may conceive what a laugh there be against he for he have relate the circumstance of he find it to several of the company before they sit down to supper this remind I of a anecdote mention by brantôme as have occur at milan in he time a glove be in this case also the cause of the _ désagrément _ a married lady have be much court by a spanish cavalier of the name of leon : one day think he have make sure of she he follow she into she bedroom but meet with a severe and decide repulse and be compel to leave she _ re infectà _ in he confusion he leave one of he glove on the bed which remain there unperceived by the lady the husband of the lady arrive shortly afterwards and as he be aware of the attention of the spaniard to he wife and have notice he go into the house he go directly to he wife 's chamber where the first thing that captivate he attention be a man 's military glove on the bed he however say nothing but from that moment abstain from all conjugal duty the lady finding herself thus neglect by a husband who have be formerly tender and attentive be at a loss to know the reason and determine to come to a _ éclaircissement _ with he in as delicate a manner as she could she therefore take a slip of paper write the follow line thereon and place it on he table : _ vigna era vigna son era podada or più non son e non sò per qual cagion non mi poda il mio patron _ -lrb- 103 -rrb- the husband on read these line write the follow in answer : _ vigna erus vigna seus erus podada e più non seus per la gran fa del leon non ti poda il tuo patron _ the lady on read these line perceive at once the cause of she husband 's estrangement and succeed in explain the matter satisfactorily to he which be facilitate by the ingenuous declaration of leon himself that he have try to succeed but have be repulse the husband and wife be perfectly reconcile live happily and no doubt the vine be cultivate as usual i leave florence the 27th November and arrive at turin 5th December in a evil hour i engage myself to accompany a old swiss baroness with whom i become acquaint at the hotel of mine hembert to accompany she to turin she have with she she son a fine boy of thirteen year of age but very much spoil we engage a _ vetturino _ to conduct we to turin stop one day at milan the baroness do not speak italian and generally send for I to interpret for she when any dispute occur between she and the people at the inn and these dispute be tolerably frequent as she always give the servant wherever she stop a good deal of trouble and on depart generally forget to give they the _ buona grazia _ i sometimes pay they for she myself in order to avoid noise and tumult at other time we depart under volly of abuse and imprecation such as _ brutta vecchia maladetta carogna _ and so forth the baroness have strong aristocratic prejudice and be a bitter enemy of the french revolution to which she attribute collectively all the _ désagrémens _ she have experience during life and all the inconvenience she meet with during we present journey the negligence and impertinence of the servant in italy be invariably attribute by she to the revolutionary principle and she tell I that the servant in she native canton bern be the best in the world but that even in they the french revolution have make a great deal of difference and that they be not so submissive as they use to be as she send for I to be she dragoman in all she dispute on the road you may conceive how glad i be to arrive at turin to be rid of she she put I in mind of gabrina in the _ orlando furioso _ we stop one day at milan but we be very near be detain two or three day at fiacenza owing to a informality in the baroness 's passport which have not be visé by the austrian legation at florence in vain she plead that she be tell at the inn at florence that such _ visa _ be not necessary the police officer at the austrian _ douane _ at a short distance beyond piacenza be inexorable and refuse to _ viser _ she passport to allow she to proceed she be in a sad dilemma and it be think we should be oblige to remain at piacenza i however recommend she to be guide by I and not to talk with or scold anybody and that i would ensure she arrival at milan without difficulty for i have observe that she scolding the officer at the _ douane _ only serve to make he more obstinate i recommend she therefore that when we should arrive within sixty or seventy pace of the gate at milan she should get out of the carriage with she son and walk thro ' the gate on foot with the utmost unconcern as if she belong to the town and be return from a promenade and that while they stop we who be in the carriage to examine we passport she should walk direct to the inn where we be to lodge then write to the consul of she nation to explain the business she follow my advice and pass unobserved and unmolested into milan on the precede evening at castel-puster-lengo at supper i ask whether she think the rigor of the austrian government be also the offspring of the french revolution the baroness have bring up she son in all these feeling and particularly in a determine hatred of the canton de vaud for in the evening when we arrive at the inn and be sit round the fire he would shake the burning faggot about and say : _ voilà la ville de lausanne en cendre _ if he grow up with these idea and act upon they he stand a good chance of be shoot in a duel by some vaudois it be a pity to see a child so spoil for he be a very fine boy tho ' very violent in he temper which probably he inherit from he mother somebody at the _ pension surpe _ at milan who know she tell I that the baroness be of a aristocratic family and have marry a rich _ bourgeois _ of bern whom she treat rather too much _ de haut en bas _ in short that it be a marriage quite _ à la george dandin _ till the poor man take it into he head to die one day at turin we part company she for genoa and i for lausanne _ from turin to lausanne _ i feel the cold very sensibly in the journey from florence to milan and turin there be not a colder country in europe than lombardy in the winter the vicinity of the alp contribute much to this and the house be exceedingly large and have no stove it be quite impossible that the fireplace can give heat sufficient to warm the room i start from turin on the morning of the 9th December in the french diligence bind to lyon but take my place only as far as chambéry in the diligence be a piedmontese colonel who have serve under napoleon and a young scotchman a relation of lord minto the latter be fond of excursion in ice and snow and on we arrival at suza he propose to I to start from there two or three hour before the diligence and to ascend mont ceni on foot as far as the _ hospice _ and i be mad enough to accede to the proposal for it certainly be little less than madness in a person of my chilly habit and susceptibility of cold and who have pass several year within the tropics to scale the alp on foot in the middle of December and to walk 24 mile in snow and ice at one o'clock in the morning which be the hour at which we start i be well clad in flannel and i go thro ' the journey valiantly and in high spirit and without suffer much from the cold till within five mile of the hospice when a heavy snow storm come on it then begin to look a little ugly and but for napoleon 's grand _ chaussès _ we be lose we struggle on three mile further in the snow before we fall in with a _ maison de refuge _ we knock there and nobody answer we then determine _ coûte que coûte _ to push on to the _ hospice _ which we know could not be more than two mile distant indeed it be much more advisable so to do than to run the risk of be freeze by remain two or three hour in the cold air till the diligence should come up in standing still i begin to feel the cold bitterly so in spite of the snow storm we push on and arrive at the inn at mont-ceni at five in the morning we rub we hand and face well with snow and take care not to approach the fire for several minute fortify ourselves in the interim with a glass of brandy we then have some coffee make and lay ourselves down to sleep by the side of a enormous fire until the diligence arrive which make its appearance at eight o'clock the passenger stop to breakfast and the scotchman propose to I to make the descent of lans-le-bourg also on foot but i be quite satisfied with the prowess i have already exhibit and decline the challenge he however set off alone and thus perform the entire passage of mont ceni on foot as for the rest of we we be carry down on a _ traineau _ that be to say the diligence be unloaded and its wheel take off the baggage and wheel be put on one _ traineau _ and the diligence with the passenger in it on another and in this manner we descend to lans-le-bourg nothing remarkable occur on this journey and we arrive at chambéry in good case i hire a _ calèche _ to go to geneva remain there three day and arrive at lausanne on the 18th December -lrb- 100 -rrb- i start from lausanne on the 4th march 1817 and arrive on the same day at 4 o'clock at geneva on my arrival at geneva my banker inform I that i have be denounce to the police for some political opinion i have speak at the _ hôtel de l'ecu de genéve _ previous to my journey into italy and that i have be trace as far as turin i go directly on hearing this to the police and desire to know who my accuser be and that the accusation against I might be investigate immediately both these proposition be however decline and i be tell it be a _ affaire passeé _ and of no sort of consequence so that from that day to this i have never be able to ascertain who my friend be i leave lausanne with the intention of pay a visit to my friend col wardle and he family at clermont-ferrand in the department of the puy de dôme in auvergne where they be reside i staid three day at geneva and then set off at 7 in the evening on the 8th march with the courier for lyon i never regret any thing so much and be near pay severely for my rashness in put myself into such a wretched conveyance at such a season of the year but i have make the agreement with the courier without inspect he carriage and be oblige to adhere to the bargain it be a vehicle entirely open before it be a bitter cold rainy snowy night and i have the rain and snow in my face the whole way and on cross the cerdon i be seize with a violent ague fit and suffer so much from it that on arrival at a village beyond nantua where we stop for supper i determine to proceed no further but to rest there that night and i ask the innkeeper if he could furnish I with a bed for the night he however make so many objection and seem so unwilling that i should remain that i be oblige to make up my mind to proceed i allay the _ frissonnement _ by a large glass of brandy and water make fiery hot at eight o'clock next morning i arrive at lyon more dead than alive a warm bath however remain in bed the whole day bury in blanket abstain from all food a few grain of calomel at night and copious libation of rice gruel the next day restore I completely to health and after a _ séjour _ of four day at lyon i be enable to proceed on my journey to clermont on the 14th march we arrive at roanne in the evening and i stop there the whole night between lyon and roanne be the mountain of tarare where the road be cut right athwart the mountain and be consequently terribly steep indeed it be the steepest ascent for a carriage i ever behold all the passenger be oblige to _ bundle out _ and ascend on foot and even then it be a most arduous _ montée _ for such a cumbrous machine as a french diligence the country between lyon and roanne appear diversified but this be not the season for enjoy the beauty of nature roanne consist of one immensely long street but it be broad and contain excellently build house and shop there be a theater also and bath it be situate on the loire which i now salute for the first time the follow morning at nine o'clock a _ patache _ -lrb- a sort of two wheel carriage -rrb- be in wait to convey I the remainder of my journey and i arrive at night at a large village or town call thier halfway between roanne and thier on stop at a small village to dine i observe a dish of frog at the kitchen fire at the inn and as it be the first time i have observe they as a article of food in france i be desirous to taste they they be dress in a _ fricassée _ of white sauce and i find they excellent the leg only be use they would be delicious as a curry the next morning we continue we journey and cross the river allier at twelve o'clock arrive at clermont-ferrand at 2 pm and dine with col wardle clermont and ferrand be two town within a mile and half distant from each other and this clermont be generally call clermont-ferrand to distinguish it from other town of the same name clermont march 26th i have take lodgings for a month and board with a french family for 90 frank per month on the road hither the immense mountain call the puy de dôme be discernible at a great distance it be say to have be a volcano clermont be a very ancient city and have a air of dullness but the _ place _ and promenade round the town be excellent it be the capital of this department -lrb- puy de dôme -rrb- there be a terrible custom here of empty the _ aguas mayores y menores _ -lrb- as the spaniard term those secretion -rrb- into the small street that lie at the back of the house the consequence be that they be clog up with filth and there be always a most abominable stench one must be careful how one walk thro ' these street at night from the liability of be salute by a golden shower the lower class of the auvergnat have the reputation of be dirty slovenly and idle here be a church build by the english in the time of edward iii when the black prince command in this country and it be in a chapel in this city the remains of which still exist that peter the hermit preach the first crusade these be almost the only thing worthy of remark in the town itself except that there be a good deal of commerce carry on manufacture of crockery cloth and silk stocking but in the natural curiosity of the environs of clermont there be a great deal to interest the botanist and mineralogist and above all there be a remarkable petrify well very near the town where by leave piece of wood shell-fish and other article expose to the drop of the water they become petrified in a short time this water have the same effect on dead animal and rapidly convert they into stone i have myself see a small basket fill with plover ' egg become in eight day a perfect petrifaction clermont April 2d i be arrive here at rather a dull season : the carnaval be just over and all the young lady be take to they _ livre d'heure _ to atone for any levity or indiscretion they may have be guilty of during the hey day of the carnaval the wardle family have a very pleasant acquaintance here chiefly among the _ libéraux _ or moderate royalist but there be some most inveterate _ ultra _ in this city who keep aloof from any person of liberal principle as they would of a person infect with the plague the noblesse of auvergne have the reputation of be in general ignorant and despotic there be but little _ agrément _ or instruction to be derive from they society for they have not the idea of the age in general the noble of auvergne tho ' great stickler for feudality and for they privilege and tho ' they dislike the revolution have the good sense not to emigrate there be a swiss regiment of two battalion quarter here it bear the name of its colonel de sali as there be a number of officer of the old army here on half pay about three hundred in number it be say frequent dispute occur between they and the swiss officer the swiss be look upon by the people at large as the satellite of despotism and not without reason it be i think degrade for any country to have foreign troops in pay in time of peace several attempt have be make in the chamber of deputy to obtain they removal or _ licencíement _ but without success as it be suppose that the song of the _ ranz des vaches _ affect the sensibility of the swiss very much and make they long to return to they native mountain a wag have recommend to all the young lady in france who be musician to play and sing the _ ranz des vaches _ with all they might in order to induce the swiss to betake themselves to they native country there have be a great deal of denunciation go forward here but the general de v -- -lrb- 104 -rrb- who command the troops in clermont determine to put a stop to it he have the good sense to see that such a system if encourage would be destructive of all society prejudicial to the government and vexatious to himself as he would be thereby keep continually in hot water accordingly on a delator present himself and accuse another of not be well affect to the present order of thing and of have speak disrespectfully of the king m de v -- say to he : i have no doubt sir that you denunciation proceed from pure motive and i give you full credit for you zeal and attachment to the royal cause but i can not take any step against the person whom you accuse unless you be willing to give I leave to publish you name and consent to be confront with he so that i may examine fairly the state of the case and render justice to both party the accuser decline accede to this proposition the general desire he to withdraw and shortly after intimate publicly that he would listen to no denunciation unless the denouncer give up he name and consent to be confront with the accuse the consequence of this intimation be that all denunciation cease the late prefect however be not so prudent and choose rather to encourage delation but mark the consequence he arrest several person wrongfully be oblige to release they afterwards be in continual hot water and it end by the government be oblige to displace he to avoid the merit vengeance of many individual whom he have ill-treat he be oblige on give up he prefecture to make a precipitate retreat from clermont the delator attempt the same system with the new prefect and col wardle have invite some of the swiss officer to a ball to which be likewise invite people of all opinion a information be lodge against he purport that he want to corrupt the swiss officer from they allegiance the prefect send the letter to col wardle and say that it have not make the slightest impression on he mind and that he treat it as a malicious report the new prefect adopt the same system as the general and tranquillity be since perfectly restore thing have be take a better turn since the dissolution of the _ chambre introuvable _ decaze the present minister be a able man and if he be not _ contrarié _ by the _ libéraux _ he will keep the fanatical _ ultra _ in good order the bishop of clermont be a liberal man also and as it seem the wish of the present public functionary here to conciliate it be to be hope that they example will not be lose on the _ bon vieux gentilshomme _ of auvergne i find a inexhaustible fund of entertainment from the conversation of m c -- he have so many interesting anecdote to relate respect the french revolution with regard to he present occupation which be direct towards rural economy he tell I that he have succeed in a plan of cleanse the town from its augean filth and make it very profitable to himself and that he calculate to obtain a revenue thereby of twenty thousand frank annually he have in short undertake to be the grand _ scavenger _ of the town and the government in addition to a salary of 2500 franc per annum which they give he for he trouble give to he the exclusive privilege of remove all the dung he can collect in the precinct of the city and of convert it to he own advantage he begin by fitting up a large enclosure wall on each side and in which he deposit all the filth he can collect in the stable yard and street of clermont he send he cart round the town every morning to get they load all they contents be bring to this repository and shoot out there straw be then place over this dung and then earth or soil collect from gully and ravine and this arrange _ stratum super stratum _ till it form a immense compact cake of rich compost and when it have fill one of the yard and have complete a thickness of five foot he sell it to the farmer who send they cart to carry it off he have divide this enclosure or repository into three or four compartment the compost therefore be prepared and ready to be carry off in one yard while the other be fill in this he have render a great benefit to the public for the auvergnat be incurable in they custom of empty they _ pot de chambre _ out of the window so that the street every morning be in a terrible state : but thanks to the industry of c -- he car go round to collect the precious material and all be clear away by twelve o'clock he collect bone too and offal to add to the compost he conduct I to see he premise but the odour be too strong i return to lausanne by the same route leave clermont on the 6th April stay four day at lyon and as many at geneva young wardle accompany I we meet with no other adventure on the road than have a young catholic priest fresh from the seminary for we travel companion from thier to roanne this young man wish to convert wardle and myself to catholicism among many argument that he make use of be that most silly one which have be so often sport by the catholic theologian viz : that it be much safer to be a catholic than a protestant inasmuch as the catholic do not allow that any person can be save out of the pale of they church whereas the protestant do allow that a catholic may be save i answer he that this very argument make more against catholicism than any other and that this intolerant spirit would ever prevent I -lrb- even have such a idea enter into my head -rrb- of embrace such a religion i then tell he that once for all i do not wish to enter into any theological dispute that i have fully make up my mind on these subject and that i would rather take the opinion of a voltaire or a franklin on these matter than all the opinion of all the theologian and churchman that ever sit in council from the council of nicsea to the present day this silence he effectually such be the absurd line of conduct pursue by the catholic priest of the present day in france instead of reform the discipline and dogma of they church and adapt it to the enlighten idea of the present age they be sedulously employd in preach intolerant doctrine and revive absurd legend and pretend miracle which have be long ago consign to contempt and oblivion by all rational catholic and by this they hope to re-establish the ecclesiastical power in its former glory and preponderance vain hope by the american and french revolution a great light be go up to the _ gentile _ catholicism be on its last leg and they might as soon attempt to replace we old friend and school acquaintance jupiter on the throne of heaven as to re-establish the papal power in its pristine splendor to borrow the language of the _ pilgrim 's progress _ the giant _ pope _ will be soon as dead as the giant _ pagan _ on arrival at lyon we put up at the _ hôtel du parc _ where i find cheaper and better entertainment than at the _ hôtel du nord _ my friend young wardle have fall in love with a very beautiful _ cafetière _ at lyon ' and spend a great part of he time in the _ café _ at which this nymph administer and look at she _ sigh look and sigh again _ it be not probable however that he will succeed in he suit for she have be court by very many other and no one have succeed she remain constant to she _ good man _ and the breath of calumny have never venture to assail she i meet one day at lyon with my old friend w -- s of strassburg who be a lieutenant in the 25th regiment in the french service and serve in the battle of waterloo -lrb- 105 -rrb- he be now here and be on _ demi-solde _ employ himself in a mercantile house here as principal commi he dine with we and we pass a most pleasant day together i arrive on the 20th April at lausanne \* \* \* \* \* after remain some week at lausanne on my return from clermont i determind on make a pedestrian trip as far as bern and neufchatel previous to return into italy which it be my intention to do in September i send on my portmanteau accordingly to payerne near avench intend to pay a visit and pass three day with my friend the revd mr j -lrb- ominus -rrb- -lrb- 106 -rrb- the rector of the parish there from whom i have receive a press invitation i be acquaint at lausanne with he daughter mme c -- and be much pleased in she society she have great talent of conversation and i never in my life meet with a lady possess of so much historical knowledge i start on the 27th June from lausanne pass the first night at mondon and the next afternoon arrive at avench the _ aventicum _ of the ancient roman payerne be only a mile distant from avench and i be receive with the utmost cordiality by the worthy pastor and he daughter the scenery on the road to avench be very like the scenery in all the rest of the canton de vaud viz alternate mountain and valley lofty tree and every spot capable of cultivation bear some kind of produce corn just ready for the sickle and fruit such as cherry and strawberry in full bloom avench have a air of great antiquity and look very gloomy withal which form a striking contrast to the neat well build town and village of this canton on the bank of the lake leman where everything appear so stir and cheerful avench on the contrary be very dull and there be little society at mr j -lrb- ominus -rrb- there be besides he daughter he son and he son 's wife all the _ ministre _ -lrb- for such be the word in use to designate protestant clergyman and you would give great offence be you to call they _ prêtres _ -rrb- have a fix salary of 100 # sterling per annum with a house and ground attach to the cure so that by farm a little they can maintain then family creditably m jominus lose he wife some time ago and still remain a widower i leave payerne on the fifth of July and walk to the _ campagne _ of m de t -lrb- reytorre -rrb- we -lrb- 107 -rrb- situate on the bank of the lake morat it be a very pretty country house spacious and roomy and i be receive with the utmost cordiality by m de t -lrb- reytorren -rrb- and he amiable family he be a very opulent proprietor in this part of the country and have spend part of he life in england he be a dignified look man a little too much perhaps of the old school and no friend to the innovation and change arise from the french revolution have live much among the tory nobility of england he have imbibe they idea and view of thing he son be now employ in one of the public office in london he wife and three daughter one of whom be marry to a _ ministre _ dwell with he with this family i pass three day in the most agreeable manner i find the style and manner of living of the _ noblesse _ -lrb- or country gentleman as we should style they -rrb- of switzerland very comfortable in every sense of the word i wish my friend the french would take more to a country life it would essentially benefit the nation the way of living in m de t -lrb- reytorre -rrb- we family be as follow a breakfast of coffee and bread and butter be serve up to each person separately in they own room or in the _ salle à manger _ before dinner every one follow he own avocation or amusement at one the family assemble to dinner which generally consist of soup _ bouillus entrées _ of fish flesh and fowl _ entremet _ of vegetable a _ rôti _ of butcher 's meat fowl or game pastry and desert the wine of the country be drunk at dinner as a table wine and _ old _ wine of the country or wine of foreign growth be hand round to each guest during the desert after dinner coffee and liqueur be serve after a hour 's conversation or repose promenade be propose which occupy the time till dusk music card or reading play fill up the rest of the evening till supper be announce at nine o'clock which be generally as substantial as the dinner on take leave of mr de t -lrb- reytorre -rrb- n ' family i walk to the bank of the lake neufchâtel have a stout fellow with I to carry my _ sac-de nuit _ on arrival at the lake i cross over in a boat to neufchâtel which lie on the other side i remain there the whole of the day it be a very pretty neat little city in a romantic position its government be a complete anomaly neufchâtel form a component part of the helvetic confederacy and yet the inhabitant be vassal of the king of prussium and the aristocracy be proud of this badge of servitude the king of prussium however do not at all interfere with its internal government and he supremacy be in no other respects useful to he than in give he a slight revenue french be the language speak in the canton there be a marked distinction of rank all over switzerland except in geneva vaud and the small democratic canton such as zug and schwytz where it be merely nominal in short tranquillity be the order of the day each rank respect the privilege of the other and the peasant however rich be not at all disposed to vary from he usual mode of life or to ape the noble and hence tho ' sumptuary law be no longer in force they continue so virtually and the peasantry in all the german canton adhere strictly to the national costume bern 14 July i put myself in the diligence that ply between neufchatel and bern at nine pm on the 12 July and the follow morning put up at the _ crown inn _ in the city of bern in the _ pay allemand _ whereas the french canton be term the _ pay romand _ bern be a remarkably elegant city as much so as any in italy and much cleaner withal the street be broad and in most of they be _ trottoir _ under arcade there be a great number of book-seller here and the best edition of the german author be to be procure very cheap bern be situate on a eminence form almost a island as it be in the middle of the river aar steep ravine be on all side of it and there be a bridge over the aar to keep up the communication and as the border of the island on which the city stand be very steep a zig-zag road wind along the ravine bring you to the city gate these gate be very superb on each side of the gate be two enormous white stone bear the emblem of the tutelary genius of this city the house be very lofty and solidly build the promenade in the environs of bern be the finest i have see anywhere and the grounds allot to this purpose be very tastefully lay out these promenade be pave with gravel and cut thro ' the forest that lie on the _ coteaux _ and ravine on the other side of the aar there be several neat villa in the neighborhood of these promenade and there be _ cafés _ and _ restaurant _ for those who chuse to refresh themselves such be the beauty of these walk that one feel inclined to pass the whole day among they they be lay out in such variety and be so multiply that you often lose you way you be sure however to be bring up by a _ point de vue _ at one or other of the angle of the zig-zag and this serve as a guide _ pour vous orienter _ as the french say another favorite promenade be a garden in the town itself that environ the whole city from which and from the superb terrace of the cathedral you have a magnificent view of the glacier that tower above the grindelwald and lauterbrunn the immense forest that be in the neighborhood of bern form a striking contrast with the cornfield in the vally and on the _ coteaw _ there be but few vineyard in the neighborhood of bern bern 16 July the diet be hold this year in bern and it be now sit i have meet with the two deputy of the canton de vaud mm p ----- and m ----- i be glad to hear from they that the animosity exist between the two canton of bern and vaud be begin to subside m p ------ have make a most able and conciliate speech at the diet still there be a good deal of jealousy rankle in the breast of the bern _ noblesse _ and the _ avulsumimperium _ be a very sore subject with they i recollect once at lausanne meeting with a young man of one of the principal family of bern who have be hi the english service the conversation happen to turn on the emancipation of the canton de vaud from the domination of bern when the young man become perfectly furious and insist that the vaudoi have no right whatever to they liberty for that the canton of bern have purchase the province of vaud from the duke of savoy _ en un mot -lrb- say he -rrb- ils sont nos esclaves nos ilotes et ils sont aussi clairement notre propriété que les nègres de la jamaïque le sont de leurs maîtres _ a very harsh measure have lately be pass in the diet evidently suggest by the aristocracy of bern which tend to fine and punish those swiss officer who remain in prance to serve under napoleon after he return from elba and who do not obey the order of the diet which recall they a very able objection have be make to this measure in a _ brochure _ wherein it be state that many of these officer have no means of live out of france and that on a former occasion when a number of swiss officer be serve the english government and be employ in america in the war against the united state in 1812 and 1818 the diet then under napoleon 's influence issue a decree recall they and command they to quit the english service forthwith this they refuse to do and continue to serve no notice whatever be take of this act of disobedience when they return to they native country on be disband in 1814 and they be very favourably receive why then say the author of this pamphlet be a similar act of disobedience to pass unnoticed in one instance and to be so severely punish in another or do you wish to prove that you vengeance be direct only against those who remain in france to fight for its liberty when invade by a foreign foe while those who remain in america to fight against the liberty and existence of the american republic you have receive with applause and congratulation be such conduct worthy of republican o fie such a argument be in my opinion convincing for all the world except for a english tory a french _ ultra _ or a bern oligarch the arsenal here be well worth see here be a superb collection of ancient armor much of which be the spoil of the austrian and burgundian chivalry who fall in they attempt to crush helvetic liberty by way of shew how fond the bernoi be of old institution and custom they have be at the trouble to catch three or four bear and keep they in a walled pit in the city where they be well feed and take care of the popular superstition be that the bear entertain in this manner contribute to the safety of the commonwealth and this establishment continue ever in full force until the dissolution of the old confederacy take place and the establishment in its place of the helvetic republic under the influence of the french directorial government the custom then appear absurd and useless be abolish and the bear be sell but since the peace of 1814 other bear have be catch and be nourishd as the former one be at the expence of the state bern derive its name from _ büren _ the german word for _ bear _ -lrb- plural number -rrb- only the french spell _ berne _ with a _ e _ at the end of it there be no theatrical amusement go forward here card and now and then a little music form the evening recreation in the inn at bern i become acquaint with a most delightful milanese lady and she son she name be l ------ she be the widow of a opulent banker at milan and have a large family of child she be about thirty-eight year of age and be still a remarkably handsome woman time have make very little impression on she and she unite very please manners with a great taste for litterature she be greatly proficient in the english language and litterature which she understand thoroughly tho ' she speak it with difficulty she be a enthusiastic admirer of shakespeare milton and byron she have be to zurich for she son who be employ in a commercial house there in order to take he back with she into italy she speak french as well as italian and she son have a very good knowledge of german she offer I a seat in she carriage on the understanding that i be go to lausanne where she intend to stop a day or two a offer of the kind make by so elegant and fascinating a woman you may be assure i do not scruple to accept and i be in hope of improve on this acquaintance and renew it at milan indeed do not business oblige I to remain some week at lausanne i should certainly offer my service to escort she all the way to milan she have letter of introduction for lausanne and during she stay there i act as she _ cicerone _ to point out the most interesting object and point of view which the place afford -lrb- 104 -rrb- loui charle joseph gravier vicomte de vergennes d'alonné be the son of the comte de vergenne who be minister under the reign see no bound to the horizon she be apprehensive of _ fall down _ and _ rolling over _ she remark remind I of one of the objection make to the project of columbus 's voyage in discovery of a western passage to india it be say that in consequence of the rotundity of the earth they would roll down and never be able to get up again the sensation experience by my fellow traveller however may be well likewise make two very pleasant acquaintance the one a portuguese the other a milanese the milanese be a cousin of the neapolitan minister di m ------ and the portuguese -lrb- m de n ------ -rrb- have take a escort as far as _ torre tre pontus _ be oblige to start very early from velletrus in order to reach terracina before night-fall nothing however occur and we arrive at terracina without accident the rascally innkeeper there make mr o ------ pay forty frank for each miserable room that he occupy and fifteen frank a head for he supper he be very insolent with all i be rejoice to find that in one instance he fail in he hope of extortion as he be oblige by law to furnish supper and bed at a fix price to those who travel with _ vetturinus _ and be _ spesatus _ he whenever a _ vetturino _ arrive lock up all he decent chamber and say that they be engage in order to keep they for those traveller who may arrive in they own carriage and whom he can fleece _ ad libitum _ a friend of mine and he lady who be travel in they own carriage have in order to avoid this extortion engage with a _ vetturino _ to conduct they from naple to rome with _ he horse _ but they own carriage and have stipulate to be _ spesatus _ mine host of terracina see a smart carriage drive up order one of he best room to be get ready usher they in himself and returnd in half a hour to ask what they would have for supper when to he great astonishment and mortification they refer he for the arrangement of the supper to the _ vetturino _ say that they be _ spesatus _ he then begin to curse and swear say that they should not have that room and want to turn they out of it forcibly but my friend major g -- take up one of he pistol which be lie on the table and tell the innkeeper that if he do not cease to molest they and instantly quit the room he would blow out he brain this threat have the desire effect and he withdraw it appear that this fellow have in the end outwit himself for most people now who travel on this road in they own carriage chuse to travel with a _ vetturino _ and he horse and be _ spesatus _ solely in order to avoid the extortion practice upon they we arrive at naple on the 29th October without accident a _ buona grazia _ of a _ scudo _ at the frontier obviate the delay which would otherwise have occur in examine we baggage by the _ douanier _ i the sentry either asleep or play at card with they companion -lrb- the sentry be double -rrb- both have leave they arm at the place where they be post at night i have no doubt they all fall asleep so that three or four active _ bandit _ might come and cut the throat of the whole chain of sentry in detail 30th October 1818 i have begin my course of water drinking at the fountain of sta lucium since i be here the last time the theater of st carlo have be finish and i go to visit it the second night after my arrival it be a noble theater and of immense size larger it be say than the _ scalum _ at il babiere di siviglia _ by rossinus and afterwards a superb _ ballo _ take closely from coleman 's _ blue-beard _ and arrange as a _ ballo _ by vestri the only difference lie in the costume and the the sister very fairly and appropriately the three actress who do the part of cenerentolum and she sister be all handsome but she who do cenerentolum surpass they all she be a perfect beauty and a grace i think the music of this opera would please the public taste in england rossinus seem to have banish every other musical composer from the stage i have see at the theater of san carlo the _ don giovannus _ of mozart but certainly after be accustom to the extreme vivacity of rossinus 's style the music even of the divine mozart appear to go off heavily there be too much of what the french the coldest animal in nature -rrb- when view thro ' this microscope appear to take place with the rapidity of a swiss torrent since i have be here i have once more ascended vesuvius there be no litterature among any part of the native society the upper class be sensualist the middling ignorant and superstitious with regard to the _ lazzaronus _ i do not think that they at all deserve the ill numerous and formidable a body they could easily do the neapolitan dialect have a far greater affinity to the spanish than to the tuscan and there be likewise a great many greek word in it when one of he work a very curious thing at naple be the number of public writer who compose letter and memorial in booth fit up in the street as the great majority of the people be so ignorant as to be unable the casino cover all and amply reimburse the proprietor with regard to political opinion here there be a great stagnation it cost the neapolitan too much trouble to think and reflect m ----- the a government purely national this be the reason why this sect be regard with as much jealousy by the different government of italy as the early christian use to be by the pagan emperor great proof of achille wonderful however as this act of improvise may appear it be not perhaps so much so as the mathematical faculty of a youth of eight year of age yorkshireman by birth who have lately exhibit he etiquette or _ gêne _ when once present to a family you may enter they house every evening without invitation make you bow to the master and mistress of the house enter into conversation or not as you this class i have meet with several sensible well-informed people who have be accurate observer of the time and have derive profit in point of instruction from the scene they have witness the papal government begin as most of the restore government do by displace many of these gentleman for no other fault than because they have serve under the ex-government and replace they by ecclesiastic as in the olden time but the papal government very soon discover that the whole political machine would be very soon at a stand by such a _ épuration _ and the most of they have be since reinstate consalvus the secretary of state be a very sensible man he have hard battle to fight with the _ ultra _ of rome in order to maintain in force the useful regulation introduce by the french government particularly the organization of a vigilant police and the put a stop to the murder and robbery which use formerly to be commit with impunity the french check the system of grant asylum to these vagabond altogether but on the restoration of the papal government a strong interest be make to allow asylum as formerly to criminal many of these gentry begin to think that the good old time be come again wherein they could commit with impunity the most atrocious crime and no less than eighty person be in prison at one time for murder this open the eye of the government and consalvus insist on the execution of these man and carry he point of establish a vigilant police the army too have be put on a better footing the papal troops be now clothe and discipline in the french manner and make a most respectable appearance the infantry be clothe in white the cavalry in green the cockade be white and yellow no greater proof can be give of the merit and utility of the french institution in italy than the circumstance of all the restore government be oblige by they interest -lrb- tho ' contrary to they wish and prejudice -rrb- to adopt and enforce they there be still require however a severer law for the punishment of post office defalcation simple dismissal be by no means adequate when it be consider how much mischief may ensue from such offence a very serious offence of this nature and which have make a great sensation have lately occur as all foreign letter must be frank and as the postage to england be very high one of the clerk at the post office have be in the habit of receive money for the franking of letter appropriate it to he own use and never forward the letter this create great inconvenience a number of family have never receive answer to they letter and be without the expect remittance begin to be uneasy and to complain a enquiry be institute and it be discover that the clerk above mention have be carry on this game to a great extent he use to tear the letter and throw the fragment into a closet several scrap of letter be thus discover and on be examine he make a ample confession of he practise he be merely discharge and no other punishment be indict on he i be no advocate for the punishment of death for any other crime but wilful murder but surely this fellow be worse than a robber and deserve a greater severity of punishment rome 10th February 1818 the carnaval have long since begin and this be the heaven of the roman lady on my remark to a lady that i be soon tired of it and after a day or two find it very childish she reply : _ bisogna esser donna e donna italiana per ben godere de ' piaceri del carnevale _ when i speak of the carnaval i speak of the last ten day of it which precede lend the following be the detail of the day 's amusement during the season after dinner which be always early the mask sally out and repair to the _ corso _ the window and balcony of the house be fill with spectator in and out of mask a scaffolding contain a immense number of seat be construct in the shape of a rectangle beginning at the _ piazza del popolo _ run parallel to the _ corso _ on each side and terminate near the _ piazza di venezia _ close to which be the goal of the horse race that take place in this enclosure carriage with person in they generally mask parade up and down this space in two current the one ascend the other descend the _ corso _ they be salute as they pass with shower of white comfit from the spectator on the seat of the scaffolding or from the balcony and window on each side of the street these comfit break into a white powder and bespatter the clothes of the person on whom they fall as if hair-powder have be throw on they this seem to be the grand joke of this part of the carnival after the carriage have parade about a hour a signal be give by the firing of a gun that the horse race be about to begin the carriage on the gun be fire must immediately evacuate the _ corso _ in order to leave it clear for the race some move off and _ rendezvous _ on the _ piazza del popolo _ just behind the scaffolding from the foot of which the horse start other file off by the _ via ripetta _ and take they stand on the _ piazza colonna _ the horse-race be perform by horse without rider generally five or six at a time they be each hold with a bridle or halter by a man who stand by they in order to prevent they start before the signal be give and this require no small degree of force and dexterity as the horse be exceedingly impatient to set off the mane of the horse be dress in ribband of different color to distinguish they piece of tin small bell and other noisy material be fasten to they mane and tail in order by frightening the poor animal to make they run the faster and with this view also squib and cracker be discharge at they as they pass along a second gun be the signal for start the keeper loose they hold and off go the horse the horse that arrive the first at the goal win the grand prize and there be smaller one for the two next this race be repeat four or five time till dusk and then the company separate and return home to dress they then repair to the ball at the different casino and at the conclusion of the ball supper party be form either at _ restaurant _ or at each other 's house during the time occupy in the ball and promenade as every body go mask either in character or in _ domino _ there be a fine opportunity for pair off and it be no doubt turn to account this be a pretty accurate account of a roman carnaval a great deal of wit and repartee take place among the mask and they be in general extremely well support and indeed they ought to be for there be a great sameness of character assume at every masquerade and very little novelty be strike out except perhaps by some foreigner who chus to introduce a national character of he own which be probably but little or not at all understand by the native and very often not at all well support by the foreigner himself a american gentleman once make he appearance as a indian warrior with he war-hatchet and calumet he dance the war dance which excite great astonishment he then present he calumet to a mask who not know what the ceremony mean decline it when the mohawk flourish he hatchet and give such a dreadful shriek as to set the whole company in alarm -lrb- 112 -rrb- on the whole this character be so little understand that it be look upon as a _ mauvaise plaisanterie _ the usual character be pulcinelli arlecchinus spanish grandee turk fortune teller flower girl and devil sometimes too they go in the costume of the god and goddess of the ancient mythology i observe that the english lady here prefer to appear without mask in the costume of the swiss and italian peasantry there be ceremony of the pope wash the foot of twelve poor man i do not see for i could not get into the sistine chapel where the ceremony be perform : and at the mass perform by the pope in the sistine chapel they perform these ceremony in the sistine chapel which be small instead of do they in the church of st peter 's which would contain so many people and produce a much grander effect a great many people be deprive of see the ceremony in the sistine chapel from the difficulty of get in the pope 's swiss guard attend on that day in they ancient _ costume _ with helmet cuirass and halberd these guard the entrance of the staircase lead to the chapel and they have no small trouble and difficulty in maintain order as there be always a great scuffle to get in and they be particularly importune by german visitor who think to be favor by they in speak to they in they own language vociferate _ ich bin ihr landsmann _ and hope by this to obtain a preference on Friday evening a large cross be erect before the grand altar every part of this cross be fill with lamp and at seven in the evening the whole be illuminate it have a most brilliant appearance and give the happiest _ chiaro-oscuro _ effect to the statue column and pilaster which abound in this vast temple there be no other light on this occasion than that reflect from the cross on easter Sunday when the pope celebrate high mass in the church of st peter 's the papal noble guard compose of young man from the principal family in rome form a hedge on each side of the nave of the church from the entrance of the facade to the grand altar the street or interval form between this double line may be about thirty foot broad and behind this guard or in any other part of the church the spectator may stand but as these guard wear very large feather in they hat they intercept very much the sight of those who stand behind they the uniform of the papal noble guard be very splendid be a scarlet coat cover with gold lace white feather white breeches and long military boot the approach of the pope be announce by the thunder of cannon and he be bring into the church dress in full pontificals with the triple crown on he head on a chair bear by man _ palanquin _ fashion he be conduct thro ' the lane form by the papal guard and as he pass he make the sign of the cross several time with he finger repeat the word : _ urbus et orbi _ he be then set down with he face front the baldachin when he immediately take off the tiara and begin the ceremony that end he leave the church in the same state and then ascend the staircase in order to prepare to give the benediction which be usually give from a window above the facade of the church the pope be there seat on a chair with the triple crown on he head troops of cavalry and infantry be draw up in a semi-circle before the façade of the church and the whole vast _ arena _ of the _ piazza di san pietro _ be cover with spectator on a sudden he holiness rise extend he hand towards heaven then spread they open and seem as if he scatter something he hold in they on the crowd below a silly young frenchman who be stand next to I say : _ le voilà le voilà qui arrache la bénédiction au ciel et qui la répand sur tout le monde _ i could not refrain from laugh at this sally tho ' i be much impressed with the solemnity of the scene which i think one of the grandest and most sublime i ever behold this ceremony conclude salve of ordnance be fire the pope retire amidst cloud of smoke and seem to vanish from the earth the troops then fire a _ feu de joie _ and move off play a march in quick time and the company disperse it be the étiquette on these occasion that no person be admit either into the church of st peter or into the sistine chapel except in full toilette the lady dress generally in black with cap and feather the gentleman either in black full dress or in military uniform from the variety of foreigner of all nation that be here most of whom be military man or intitle to wear military uniform much be add to the splendor of the spectacle on the evening of easter Monday i be present at the illumination of the facade of st peter 's row of lamp be suspend the whole length of the column and pilaster and all over the cupola so that when illuminate the style of the architecture be perceptible the illumination take place almost at once how it be manage i can not say but a splendid illuminated temple seem at once to drop from the cloud like the work of a enchanter i say _ drop from the cloud _ because the illumination begin from the cross and cupola and be communicate with the rapidity of lightning to every other part of the edifice about ten o'clock the same evening the most magnificent firework perhaps in the world begin to play from the castle of st angelo all kind of shape be assume by these firework : here be castle pagoda dragon griffin etc these last about a hour and then conclude and with they conclude all the ceremony use in commemoration of the crucifixion and resurrection of jesus christ among the sight of rome i must not omit that of a famous robber of the name of barbone who be the terror of the whole surrounding country from the depredation he commit have capitulate and surrender himself to the papal government he be now confine in the castle of st angelo as a state prisoner he wife or a woman call herself so be confine there with he and she be say to be a woman of uncommon beauty it be quite the rage among the english here to go to see these _ illustrious _ captive and madame barbone superbly dress receive the hommage of the visitor the duchess of d -lrb- evonshire -rrb- be say to have visit she and make she a present of a pearl necklace i hope this be not true surely the duchess who be a woman of talent and a encourager of the fine art might have find some other object worthier of she munificence what claim the mistress or even the wife of a public robber can have on the generosity of traveller i be at a loss to conceive but such be the _ bizarrerie _ and _ inconsequence _ of the english and no doubt be this story of she grace of d -lrb- evonshire -rrb- have give a present true or not it will occasion many other present be make to the captive princess by a host of silly lord-aping english man and woman barbone have it be say make a excellent capitulation he have stipulate to be release from prison after a year and a day 's confinement and no doubt he will then resume he old trade of brigandage in the meantime he have disband he troops as he call they but will he troops obey he now that he be a captive will they not rather chuse another leader in the time of the french occupation nothing of this kind take place but the present government be weak and timid i have not be myself to see either barbone or he wife but i have hear quite enough about they they form one of the principal sight in rome and i be quite _ unfashionable _ in not have go to visit they for accord to the opinion of my english acquaintance he who have not see barbone and he wife have see nothing \* \* \* \* \* i start from rome on the second of April with a _ vetturino _ and on arrival at baccano city of veii the follow day at ten o'clock we reach the small town of narnus here be the remains of a beautiful bridge construct over the ravine thro ' which flow the river nera and which be build in the time of augustus it afford a very favorable specimen of the roman bridge architecture there be a small chapel here and it contain engrave on a stone a description of a miracle work here about four year ago by the virgin mary who save the life of a postillion he go into the river to water he horse when he be carry off by the torrent and would have be drown have not the virgin on she aid be traveller and myself -rrb- to visit the famous cascade of the velino about three mile distant from the town of ternus the road thither be very rugged and be a continual ascent on the flank of a ravine for a long time before you arrive on the brink of the cascade you hear the roaring of the water and it certainly be the most magnificent and awe-inspiring sight of the kind i ever behold it be far more stupendous than any cascade in switzerland that of tivolus compare to it be as a infant six month old to a goliath the velino form three successive fall and the last be tremendous since it fall from a height of 1068 foot into the abyss below the foam and the froth it occasion be terrific and the spray ascend so high that in stand at the distance of fifty yard from the fall you become as wet as if you have be stand in a shower of rain the first fall it form be of 800 foot the second little less the third i have state already no painting can possibly give a faithful delineation of this and very possibly no poetic description can give a adequate idea thereof we pass the whole night at ternus and the next morning we stop to dine at spoleto the same evening we arrive at foligno spoleto be a neat town and well pave several ruin of ancient building be in its vicinity before you arrive there on the left of the road be a immensely high two-arched bridge there be a aqueduct likewise just outside the town we do not omit to read the inscription on the gate of the town in commemoration of the repulse of hannibal who fail in he attempt to make himself master of this city after have beat the roman near the lake trasymene the gate be call in consequence _ porta fuga _ and this gate constitute the principal glory of spoleto we be show the rum of a palace build by theodoric on leave the town just outside the gate we be shew a bridge which have lay underground for many century and have be lately discover a bridge be know to have be build here in the time of augustus and it be very probably the identical one we could only see the top and part of the parapet foligno be a large well build city neatly pave populous and commercial renowned for manufactory of paper wax and confectionary the whole road between spoleto and foligno be thro ' a beautiful valley in high cultivation there be a good deal of rich pasture ground and it be water by the river call in ancient tune
