chapter xv april-july 1818 journey from florence to pisa and from thence by the appennine to genoa -- massa-carrara -- genoa -- monument and work of art -- the genoese -- return to florence -- journey from florence through bologna and ferrara to venice -- monument to ariosto in ferrara -- a description of venice -- padua -- vicenza -- verona -- cremona -- return to milan -- the scalum theater -- verona again -- from verona to innspruck it be the custom for most traveller go to genoa to embark on board of a _ felucca _ at spezium which lie on the sea coast not far from sarzana : but i prefer to go by land and i can not conceive why anyone should expose himself to the risk inconvenience and delay of a sea passage when it be so easy to go by land thro ' the appennine i start accordingly the follow morning mount on a mule and attend by a muleteer with another mule to convey my portmanteau i find this journey neither dangerous nor difficult but on the contrary agreeable and romantic the road be only a bridle road i pay forty-eight frank for my two mule and driver and start at seven in the morning from sarzana the wild appearance of the appennine the aweful solitude and the highly picturesque point of view that present themselves at the various sinuosity of the mountain and valley the view of the sea from the height that tower above the town of oneglium and sestrus levante render this journey one of the most interesting i have ever make i stop to dine at borghetto and bring to the night at sestrus levante breakfast the next morning at rapallo and arrive the same evening at four o'clock in genoa borghetto be a little insignificant town situate in a narrow valley surround on all side by the lofty crag of the appennine sestri levante be a long and very straggling town part of it be situate on the sea shore and the other part on the gorge of the mountain descend towards the sea beach so that the former part of the town lie nearly at right angle with the latter with a considerable space intervene the road for the last four mile between borghetto and sestrus levante be a continual descent the inn be very comfortable and good at sestri levante the beginning of the road between sestrus and rapallo be on the beach till near rapallo when it strike again into the mountain and be of considerable ascent rapallo be a very neat pretty place situate on a eminence command a fine view of the sea the greater part of the road between rapallo and genoa be on the sea-coast but cut along the mountain which here form a bluff with the sea villa garden and vineyard line the whole of this route and nothing can be more beautiful the neatness of the villa and the abundance of the population form a striking contrast to the wild solitude between sarzana and sesto where -lrb- except at borghetto -rrb- there be not a house to be see and scarce a human creature to be meet and where the eagle seem to reign alone the uncontrolled lord of the creation genoa 23rd April the view of genoa from the sea be indisputably the best for on enter by land from the eastern side the rampart be so lofty as to intercept the fine view the city would otherwise afford from the sea side it rise in the shape of a amphitheatre a view therefore take from the sea give the best idea of its grandeur and of the magnificence of its building for everybody on behold this grand spectacle must allow that this city well deserve its epithet of _ superba _ i observe in my daily walk on the _ esplanade _ a number of beautiful woman the genoese woman be remarkable for they beauty and fine complexion they dress generally in white and they style of dress be spanish they wear the _ mezzara _ or veil in the management of which they display much grace and not a little coquetry instead of the fan exercise recommend to woman by the _ spectator _ the art of handle the _ mezzara _ might be reduce to a manual and teach to the lady by word of command i put up at the house of a spanish lady on the _ piazza st siro _ and here for four _ livre _ a day i be sumptuously board and lodge there be three principal street in genoa viz _ strada nuova _ _ balbus _ and _ nuovissima _ yet these three street may be properly say to form but one inasmuch as they lie very nearly in a right line these street be broad and align with the finest building in genoa this street or street be the only one that can be properly call so accord to the idea we usually attach to the word the other deserve rather the name of lane and alley tho ' exceedingly well paved and align with excellent house and shop in fact the street _ nuova _ _ nuovissima _ and _ balbus _ be the only one thro ' which carriage can pass the other be far too narrow to admit of the passage of carriage the house on each side of they be of immense height being of six or seven story which form such a shade as effectually to protect those who walk thro ' these alley from the ray of the sun the house diminish in height in proportion as they be build on the slant of the mountain from the bottom to the top those at the bottom be the loftiest carriage be scarcely of any use in the city of genoa except to drive from one end of the town to another thro ' the street _ nuova _ _ balbus _ and _ nuovissima _ and accordingly a carriage with four wheel or even with two be a rare conveyance in genoa the general mode of conveyance be on a sedan chair carry by porter or on the back of mule or ass genoa be distinguish by the beauty of the palace of its patrician which be more numerous and more magnificent than those of any other city probably in the world the ducal palace or palace of government where the doge use to reside claim my first attention yet tho ' much larger it be far less splendid than many of the palace of individual patrician in fact the ducal palace be build in the gothic taste and resemble a gothic fortress have round tower at each angle the hall where the grand council use to sit be superb and be adorn with column of _ jaune antique _ on the _ plafond _ be a painting represent the discovery of america by columbus for the genoese duly appreciate and never can forget they illustrious countryman the line of tasso _ un uom della liguria avrà ardimento _ etc and the follow stanza _ tu spiegherai colombo a urn nuovo polo _ etc be in the mouth of everyone -lrb- 117 -rrb- the hall of the petty council be neat but it be the recollection of the history of this once famous republic that render the examination of this palace so interesting but now genoa 's glory be go she have be basely betray into the hand of a government she most detest the king of sardinium be nowhere and he be not a little proud of be the possessor of such a noble sea port which enable he to rank as a maritime power the genoese be laborious and make excellent sailor but now there be nothing to animate they and they will never exert themselves in the service of a domination which be so little congenial to they they sigh for they ancient government of whose glory they have so often hear and whose brilliant exploit have be hand down to the present day not merely by historical writer and poet but by _ improvisatorus _ from mouth to mouth the genoese noble those merchant king whose riches exceed at one time those of the most powerful monarch of europe who be the pawn-broker to those sovereign be now in a state of decay commerce can only flourish on the soil of liberty and take wing at the sight of military and sacerdotal chain and tho ' the present sovereign affect to caress the genoese _ noblesse _ they return he civility with sullen indifference and half conceal contempt and aversion the commerce of genoa be transfer to leghorn which increase in prosperity as the former decay the climate of genoa be say to be exceedingly mild during the winter be protect on the north by the appennine which tower above it to a immense height beautiful villa and grounds tastefully lay out in plantation of orange tree pomegranate etc abound in the environs of this city and everything announce the extreme industry of the inhabitant for the soil be proverbially barren this shew what they have do and what they could still do be they free but now they have nothing to animate they exertion the public promenade be on the bastion and curtain of the fortification on the _ esplanade _ and in the street _ balbus _ _ nuova _ and _ nuovissima _ there be also another very delightful promenade tho ' not much use by the lady viz on the molum or pier envelop the harbor one of the most remarkable construction in genoa be the bridge of carignano which be build over a immense ravine and unite the hill fengano and carignano it be so high that house of six story stand under its arch in the valley below no water except in time of flood run under this bridge and it much resemble tho ' somewhat larger the bridge at edinburgh which unite the old and new town the principal church be : first the cathedral which be not far from the ducal palace it be richly ornamented and incrust with black marble the church of the annunzia and that of st sire they be all in the gothic style of architecture and load with that variety of ornament and diversity of beautiful marble which distinguish the church of italy from those of any other country near the bridge of carignano be a church of the same name wherein be four marble colossal statue on the west of the city and run two mile along the sea-beach be the _ faubourg _ of st pietro d'arena which present a front of well build house the whole way these house be principally use as magazine and store house florence 5 may i leave genoa on the 30th April return on mule-back from genoa to sarzana stop the first night at sestrus the second evening when near sarzana it be very dark i somehow or other get out of the road and my mule fall with I into a very deep ditch but i be only slightly bruise by the fall my clothes however be cover with dirt and wet the road from genoa to sarzana might with very little expense be make fit for carriage by widen it at present it be only a bridle road and on some part of it on the side of ravine it be i think a little ticklish to trust entirely to the discretion of one 's _ monture _ at least i think so and dismount twice to pass such place on foot a wind stream be to be ford in two or three place but it be not deep except after rain and then i think it must be sometimes dangerous to pass till the water run off those who be fond of mountain scenery will like myself be highly gratify in make this journey for it be thro ' the loftiest wildest and most romantic part of the appennine from sarzana i hire a cabriolet to return to pisa and from thence i take the diligence to florence ferrara on the 9th of may i set out from florence on my journey hither two day ' journey bring I to bologna where i stop one day and the follow day i reach this place -lrb- ferrara -rrb- six mile distant from bologna the country between these two city be a perfect plain and very fertile at malalbergo -lrb- half-way -rrb- we cross the reno in a boat i put up at the _ tre morus _ in ferrara have remain two and half day here i have have time to inspect and examine almost everything of consequence that the city afford the city itself have a impose venerable appearance and can boast of some fine building yet with all this there be a air of melancholy about it it be not people in proportion to its size and grass be see grow in several of the street i believe the unhealthiness of the environ country be the cause of the decrease of population for ferrara lie on a marshy plain very liable to inundation in the center of the city stand the ancient palace of the duke of ferrara a vast gothic edifice square and flank with round tower and a large court-yard in the center it be in this court-yard that hugo and parisina be decapitate from the top of this palace a noble view of the plain of the po represent itself and you see the meanderings of that king of river as the italian poet term it as the po run thro ' a perfectly flat country and be encrease and swollen by the torrent from the alp and appennine that fall into the smaller river which unite they tributary stream with the po and accompany he as he _ seguacus _ to the adriatic this country be liable to the most dreadful inundation : flock and herd farm-house and sometimes whole village be sweep away dyke dam and canal innumerable be in consequence construct throughout this part of the country to preserve it as much as possible from such calamity ariosto 's description of a over-flowing of this river be very striking and i here transcribe it : con quel furor che il re de ' fiumi altero quando rompe tal volta argine e sponda e che ne ' campi ocnei si apre il sentiero e i grassi solchi e le biade feconde e con le sue capanne il gregge intero e co ' cani i pastor porta neil ' onde etc -lrb- 118 -rrb- even with that rage wherewith the stream that reign the king of river -- when he break he mound and make himself a way through mantuan plain -- the greasy furrow and glad harvest round and with the sheepcote nock and dog and swain bear off in he o'erwhelm water drown -- trans w rise the next place i go to see be the lyceum or university where there be a very fair cabinet of natural history in all its branch the library be very of the _ orlando furioso _ among the manuscript what gratify I most be the manuscript of the _ gerusalemme libera _ of tasso but few correction appear in this manuscript tho from the extreme polish and harmony of the versification one would expect a great many it be write in a extremely legible hand i also inspect the original manuscript of the _ pastor fido _ of guarinus and of the _ suppositus _ of ariosto i then go to visit the hospital of st anna for the sake of see the dungeon where poor tasso be confine and treat as mad for several year when one behold this wretched place where a man can scarce stand upright one only wonder how he could survive such treatment or how he could escape become insane altogether the old wooden door of this cell will soon be entirely cut away by amateur as almost everyone who visit the dungeon chop off a piece of wood from the door to keep as a relic the door be in consequence piece and repair with new wood and in a short time will be in the state of sir john cutter 's worsted stocking which be darned so often with silk that they become finally all silk ferrara have a strong citadel which be still garrison by austrian troops and they will probably not easily be induce to evacuate it the austrian eagle seldom loose he hold venice 18th may on the 16th may at six o'clock in the morning i leave ferrara in a _ cabriolet _ to go to the _ ponte di lago oscuro _ which be a large village on the south bank of the po three mile distant from ferrara a fly bridge waft I across the river which be exceedingly broad and rapid to the north bank where a barge be in wait to receive passenger for venice this barge be well fit up and supply with _ comestible _ of all sort and couch to recline on the price be twelve franc for the passage and you pay extra for refreshment the bark get under weigh at seven o'clock and descend rapidly this majestic river which however from its great breadth and from the country on each side of it be perfectly flat do not offer any interesting point of view plain and cattle grazing thereon be the only object for they take care to build the farm and house at a considerable distance from the bank on account of the inundation after have descend the po for a considerable distance we enter a canal which unite the po with the adige we then descend the adige for a short distance and enter another canal which unite the adige with the brenta here we stop to change barge and it require a hour and half to unload and reload the baggage we then enter the brenta and from thence into the lagoon and pass by the island of malamocco and chiozzo enter venice by the _ canale grande _ at three o'clock in the morning the whole night be so dark as totally to deprive we of the view of the approach of venice the barge anchor near the post office and i hire a gondola to convey I to the inn call _ le regina d'ungherium _ venice 26th may i be much strike as everyone must be who see it for the first time at the singular appearance of venice a immense city in the midst of the ocean five mile distant from any land canal instead of street gondola in lieu of carriage and horse yet it must not be infer from this that you be necessarily oblige to use a gondola in order to visit the various part of the city for its structure be as follow it be build in compartment on pile on various mud bank always cover indeed by water but very shallow and separate from each other -lrb- the mud bank i mean -rrb- by deep water on each of these compartment be build row of house each row give front to a canal the space between the back of the row of house form a narrow street or alley pave with flag stone very like cranborn alley for instance and these compartment be unite to each other -lrb- at the crossing as we should say -rrb- by means of stone bridge so that there be a series of alley connect by a series of bridge which form the _ tout ensemble _ of this city and you may thus go on foot thro ' every part of it to go on horseback would be dangerous and almost impracticable for each bridge have a flight of step for ascent and descent all this form such a perfect labyrinth from the multiplicity and similarity of the alley and bridge that it be impossible for any stranger to find he way without a guide i lose my way regularly every time that i go from my inn to the _ piazza di san marco _ which form the general rendezvous of the promenader and be the fashionable lounge of venice and every time i be oblige to hire a boy to reconduct I to my inn on this account in order to avoid this perplexity and the expence of hire a gondola every time i wish to go to the _ piazza di san marco _ i remove to another inn close to it call _ l'osterium della luna _ which stand on the bank of the _ canale grande _ and be not twenty yard from the _ piazza _ i then hire a gondola for four day successively and visit every canal and every part of the city almost every family of respectability keep a gondola which be anchor at the step of the front door of the house after the _ piazza di san marco _ of which i shall speak presently the finest building and palace of the nobility be on the bank of the _ canale grande _ which from its wind in the shape of a s have all the appearance of a river the _ rialto _ be the only bridge which connect the opposite bank of the _ canale grande _ but there be four hundred smaller bridge in venice to connect the other canal the _ rialto _ the resort of the money changer and jew be a very singular and picturesque construction being of one arch a very bold one on each side of this bridge be a range of jeweller ' shop a narrow quaus run along the bank of the _ canale grande _ i have visit several of the _ palazzo _ particularly those of the family morosinus cornaro pisanus grimanus which be very rich in marble of _ vert _ and _ jaune antique _ but they be now nearly strip of all they furniture uninhabited by they owner or let to individual mostly shopkeeper for by merchant shopkeeper chiefly jeweller and silk mercer seafaring people the constitute authority and the garrison of the place tho ' venice have fall very much into decay since the subversion of the republic as might naturally be expect and still more so since it have be under the austrian domination yet it be still a place of great wealth particularly in jewellery silk and all article of dress and luxury in the _ mercerium _ you may see as much wealth display as in cheapside or in the rue st honoré i have have the pleasure of witness a superb regatta or water _ féte _ give in honor of the visit of the archduke rainier to this city in he quality of viceroy of the lombardo-venetian kingdom there be about one hundred and fifty barge each fit up by some department of trade and commerce with allegorical device and statue richly ornamented emblematical of the trade or profession to which the barge belong each barge bear a appropriate ensign and the dress of the crew be all tasteful for ever banish from the _ piazza _ music and singing go forward in these _ casino _ and the ear be often charm with the sound of those delightful venetian air whose simple melody ravish the soul the praise can equal she merit then the delightful soul soothing music so harmonious so pathetic and the decoration so truly tasteful and classical i can never forget the impression this fascinating ballet make on I it be call _ la vestale _ it open with a view of the circus in ancient rome and various gymnastic exercise combat of gladiator of athlete and end with a chariot race with real horse the roman consul be present in all they pomp surround by lictor with axis and fasce the vestal virgin assist at this spectacle and from one of they the victor in the game receive a garland as the recompense of he prowess the victor be the son of one of the consul and the hero of the piece the heroine be the vestal virgin who crown he with the garland the young victor become desperately enamor of the vestale and she appear also to feel a incipient flame after the game be over the victor return to he father 's house and meeting there one of he friend disclose to he he love for the vestale and he idea of enter by stealth into the temple of vesta where he beloved be appoint to watch the sacred fire he friend endeavor but in vain to dissuade he from so rash a attempt which can only end in the destruction both of he beloved and himself all the remonstrance however of the friend be vain and the hero fix in he resolve watch for the opportunity when it be the turn of he beloved to officiate in the temple of vesta and enter therein the vestale be terrify and supplicate he to retire : in vain and after a long but ineffectual struggle she sink into he arm at the foot of the altar suddenly the sacred flame become extinguish a noise be hear the vestal enter the unfortunate fair be rouse from she stupor by the noise of footstep and have just time to oblige she lover to retire which he reluctantly do but not unperceived by the vestal the matron of the vestal reproach she with the crime she have commit and order she to be place in a dungeon she be bring out to be examine by the high priest find guilty and condemn by he to the usual punishment of the vestal for a breach of they vow viz the be bury alive outside the gate of rome the moment the sentence be pronounce a black veil be throw over she the scene then change to the place of execution the funeral procession take place the vault be dig and a man stand by with a pitcher of water and loaf of bread to deliver to she when she should descend the consul be present attend by the lictor and aedile all the other vestal be present of whom the culprit take a affectionate leave and be about to descend into the vault suddenly a noise of arm and shout be hear it be she lover who have collect a few follower come rush forward with arm in they hand to arrest the execution he force he way into the presence of the consul but the sight of he father inspire he with awe he stagger back at this moment a lictor at the command of the other consul plunge a spear into he breast the vestal be hurry to the brink of the vault into which she be force to descend to the accompaniment of mournful music while she die lover vainly endeavor to crawl towards she the curtain fall the exquisite acting of la pallerinus draw tear from my eye : it be indeed too horrible a subject for a _ ballo _ which in my opinion ought to end happily the scenery be the finest of the kind i think i ever witness the first scene represent the _ circus maximus _ the interior of the temple of vesta and the place of execution outside the wall of rome be most classically correct and appropriate : the music be beyond all praise and singularly affect this ballet have excite such a enthusiastic approbation that vigano the ballet master pallerinus who act the vestal and the young man who perform the hero of the piece be summon every evening after the termination of the ballet to appear on the stage and receive applause which seem to increase at every representation i have be to see this ballet six or seven time and always with increase delight i be there on the last night of its representation when some amateur and people connect with the theater put in practice what appear to mean ill-judged _ concetto _ however well merit the compliment it mean to convey when the vestal be about to descend into the vault a genius with wing rise from it and repeat a few line begin _ tu non morraus _ and tell she that the suffrage of the insubrian people have decree to she immortality and print sonnet be shower down on the stage from all part of the house i think it would have be much better to let the piece finish in the usual vienna to prague innspruck 15th July i have engage with a _ vetturino _ to convey I from verona to innspruck for four _ loui d'or _ and to be _ spesato _ a roman gentleman and he lady be my fellow traveller they be go to pass the summer month at a small _ campagne _ they possess in the tyrol we stop the first night at roveredo the road from verona to roveredo be on the bank of the adige -lrb- call in german the etsch -rrb- in a narrow and deep valley shut up on both side by mountain almost immediately on leave verona we find the weather extremely hot in this valley roveredo seem to be a very neat clean little city and the adige flow with astonishing rapidity along this narrow valley the woman of roveredo have the reputation of be very beautiful and i recollect have see two roveredo girl at venice who be model of female beauty they have a happy mixture of german and italian blood and manners but italian be the language of the country the second morning of we journey we arrive and stop to dinner at the venerable and celebrated city of trent the country we pass thro ' be much the same as that between verona and roveredo the adige be on we left trent lie also in the valley of the adige shut up between the alp the whole valley appear in high cultivation the street of trent be broad the cathedral be a remarkably fine gothic building in the church of sta marium maggiore be hold the famous council of trent there be a great many silk mill in trent german as well as italian be speak indeed the two language be equally familiar to most of the inhabitant in the evening we arrive at sabern after pass thro ' lavi one description will serve for these town and indeed for most of the town in the tyrol viz that of be neat clean and solidly build the inn be excellent and the inhabitant very civil the adige run close to the road and parallel to it nearly the whole way to bolsano or botzen where italian cease to be speak and german be the national tongue botzen be a large and flourishing place one general description will serve for the tyrol regard the town adjacent country custom inn inhabitant dress and manners first the town be fully as neat clean and well build as those in switzerland the country too be very similar tho ' not quite on so grand a scale of sublimity but you have fully as much variety in mountain and valley glacier and cascade the climate be exactly the same as that of switzerland be very hot in the valley in summer the inn be clean and good the provision excellent and well cook the wine much better than those of switzerland there be good attendance by female and all at a far cheaper rate than in switzerland the tyrolean be much more courteous in they manners than the swiss they have not that boorishness and be of more elegant figure than they helvetic neighbor the woman of the tyrol be in general remarkably beautiful exceedingly well shaped and of fine complexion in the town the bourgeoise dress well something in the french style and it be they custom to salute traveller who pass by kiss they hand to they the dress of the female peasantry however be unpleasing to the eye and so uncouth that it would make the most beautiful woman appear homely in the first place i will speak of they head dress of which there be three different kind two of which be as _ bizarre _ as can be imagine the first sort be a cap of sheepskin the fleece of which be as white as snow and the cap be of conical shape the base be exceed large in proportion to its height and resemble much the sugar loave make in egypt the second be a black scull cap with the three piece of stiff black _ gaze _ stick out like the vane of a windmill so that when put on the head one vane stand upright from the forehead and the other two from each ear the third head dress be a broad straw hat and i wish they would stick to this coiffure and discard the two other then the waist of they dress be as long as du pole antarctique a détroit de davis -lrb- 121 -rrb- they petticoat be exceedingly short scarcely reach the calf of the leg which be envelop in a pair of flame red stocking who the devil could invent such a ungraceful dress for a female the costume of the man on the contrary be become and graceful it resemble very much the costume of the andalusian the hat be exactly the same the crown be small and the rim very broad the tyrolean be a fine gallant race of man and be excellent marksman they be formerly much attach to the house of austrium but that attachment be now entirely change to dislike from the ingratitude they have meet with since they have be replace under that scepter the only fault i find in the tyrolean be that they be rather too devout and consequently too much under the influence of the clergy yet in they devotion there be not the smallest tinge of hypocrisy and they be esteem a highly moral people if you arrive at a inn in the evening while the family be at prayer neither master nor servant will come to wait on you till prayer be over and then you will be serve with sufficient alacrity but the prayer be rather long i believe the priest extort a good deal of money from these good people the road thro ' the tyrol be make by the roman in the time of septimus severus a immense number of crucifix on the road attest and command the devotion of the people how kotzebue can call innspruck a dirty town i be at a loss to conceive he must have visit it during very rainy weather for to I it appear one of the cleanest and most chearful town i have ever see there be several very fine building for instance the jesuit ' college and the franciscan monastery nothing can be more picturesque than the situation of this city in the valley of the inn and its romantic winding the suburb be very extensive and can boast several fine house the cupola of the government house be gilded which give it a splendid appearance in the _ hofkirche _ or church of the court there be a number of statue large as life in bronze among which my guide point out to I those of clovis godfrey of bouillon albert the wise charle v philip ii of spain rudolph of hapsburgh and to my great astonishment the british king arthur there be twenty-eight statue altogether but on my return to my inn i find that my guide have make a great error respect king arthur and that the say statue represent prince arthur son of henry vii king of england and not the old hero of romance and my hostess ' book further inform I that these statue be those of the king and prince belong to family connect by descent and blood with maximilian i in the same _ hofkirche _ be a fine monument erect to maximilian and a statue of bronze of this emperor be figure kneel between four bronze figure represent four virtue in the garden of the palace of the archduke ferdinand in this city be a fine equestrian statue which rest entirely on the hind foot of the horse from innspruck there be a water passage by the river inn all the way to vienna as the inn flow into the danube at take advantage of the raft which start from that place the day after to-morrow munich 20th July i leave innspruck in a _ chaise de poste _ on the 16th and arrive the same evening at five o'clock at mittenwald at a short distance before i arrive at mittenwald i enter the bavarian territory which announce itself by a turnpike gate paint white and blue the color and _ feldzeichen _ of bavarium in the austrian territory the barrier be paint black and yellow these be the characteristic color of austrium mittenwald be a small neat town offering nothing remarkable but a church yard or _ ruhe-garten _ -lrb- garden of repose -rrb- as it be call where there be a number of quaint inscription on the tombstone at mittenwald i have some trouble about my passport as it be not _ visé _ by a bavarian authority but i explain to the officer that i have never fall in with any bavarian authority since i leave rome and that while at rome i have no intention of go thro ' bavarium that at milan the austrian authority have _ visé _ my passport for vienna and that i should only pass thro ' munich without make a longer stay than one week he acquiesce in my argument but insert my explanation on the passport at half a quarter of a mile beyond mittenwald i meet the raft just about to get under weigh at eleven o'clock be this raft be about as long as the length of a thirty-six gun frigate and form of spar fasten together on this be a platform about one and a half foot high the isar begin its course close to mittenwald and the place on which the raft stand previous to departure be very shallow but water be quickly let in from sluice to float the raft and off we set with a cargo of peasant male and female and merchandise bind for munich as the river isar rush between immense mountain and form a continual descent until the plain of bavarium open to view you may conceive with what rapidity we go we encounter several fall of water of two three four and sometimes five foot which we have to _ shoot _ which no boat could possibly do without be upset the lower part of the raft be frequently under water in make these _ shoot _ and we be oblige to hold on fast to we seat to prevent be jerk off nothing can be more romantic and picturesque than this journey and there be something aweful in _ shooting _ these fall these raft be however so solidly construct that there be no danger whatever they can neither sink nor upset we arrive and halt the evening at tölz a large village or town on the right bank of the isar what give to tölz a remarkably singular appearance be that on a height at a short distance from the town and hang abruptly over the river you perceive several figure in wood larger than the life which figure form group represent the whole history of the passion of jesus christ at a short distance if you be not prepare for this you suppose that they be real man and that a procession or execution be go forward on landing i immediately ascend this hill in order to observe this curiosity and there i beheld the follow group first : christ in the midst of he disciple preach secondly : the disciple asleep in a cave and christ watching and pray next be judas betray christ to the soldiery then the judgment of christ before pilate then christ bear he cross to the place of execution and lastly the crucifixion on mount calvary the ground be curiously lay out so as to represent as much as possible the ground in the environs of jerusalem tölz be a pretty village but contain nothing more remarkable than the above group the next day at twelve o'clock we perceive the spire of munich and at two anchor close to one of the bridge from whence have hire a wheelbarrow to trundle my portmanteau i repair to the inn call the golden cross -- _ zum goldenen kreutz _ at tölz the rhetian alp recede from the view the landscape then present a sloping plain which be perfectly level within four mile of munich the river widen immediately on issue from the gorge of the tyrol and for the last five mile we be follow by boy on the bank of the river beg for wood with which we raft be laden and we throw to they many a faggot wood be the great export from the tyrol to bavaria as the latter be a flat country and have not much wood with which on the contrary the tyrol abound a sensible difference of climate be now feel and the air be keener than in the tyrol the price of a place on the raft from mittenwald to munich cost only one florin and at tölz a excellent supper bed and coffee in the morning cost I only one florin munich 23rd July munich the capital of bavarium be a ancient gothic city of venerable appearance the house be very solid in structure and the street sufficiently broad to give to the city a cheerful appearance there be some suburb add to it build in the modern taste which embellish it greatly a large place outside the old town call the _ carolinen-platz _ present a number of villa dispose in the form of a circus in these suburb the people assemble on holiday and sunday to smoke and drink beer of which a great quantity be consume it be the favorite and national beverage from the lively scene of the lower class of the bourgeoisie male and female meeting here in the _ biersschank _ and _ tanzsaale _ i be remind of the line in faust : gewiss man findet hier die schönsten mädchen und da beste bier which may be thus render : here let we halt ` tis here we be sure to find beer of the best and maiden fair and kind there be other very agreeable promenade outside the town lay out as _ jardin anglai _ the garden of ostenwald for instance and should you wish to extend you walk further there be nymphenburg a royal palace and garden just one league distant from the city the _ residenz-schloss _ or palace of the king be a solid building the interior be well worth see there be a superb saloon with a vast number of valuable miniature append to the wainscoat a enormously heavy bed groan with gold and silver embroidery and pearl and which be say to weigh a ton be to be see here there be a very good collection of picture chiefly portrait of the electoral now royal family there be a fine chapel too belong to this palace a superb staircase of marble and some fine old tapestry represent the action of otto von wittelsbach there be likewise a curious miniature copy of trajan 's column in gold and incrust with precious stone besides a variety of other thing of value there be two theater in munich one call the hof or court theater where there be a company of comedian for tragedy and comedy the expence of which be defray principally by the king the box be generally let to the nobility and the _ parterre _ be open to every body on payment i witness the representation of mozart 's _ nozze di figaro _ the king be present and be greet with much affection he have a very benignant expression of countenance he be much beloved by he subject for he have govern they paternally he have give to they a constitution _ unasked _ for they be so contented with the old government that they desire no change but he with he usual good sense see the propriety of consulting and comply with the spirit of the age a german writer of some eminence at the time of the french revolution when the aristocrat and alarmist of all country be cry out against it and propose harsh measure to arrest its progress say : sovereign of europe do you wish to set bound to the progress of french principle nothing can be more simple you have only to govern you people like maximilian of bavarium and frederick of saxony and you subject will never desire a change at the german -lrb- national -rrb- theater which be a fair size one i see a tragedy perform call _ der wald bey herman-stadt _ -lrb- the forest near hermanstadt -rrb- -lrb- 122 -rrb- it be a interesting piece take from a feudal legend the part of elisene be perform by mlle voh a very good actress i miss very much one thing in munich and that be the want of _ cafés _ like those in france and italy which have so brilliant a appearance they make coffee here at the inn and there be two or three dull place up one pair of stair where they play at billiards and make as indifferent coffee as be make in england the hour of dining at munich be in general one o'clock a slice of ham or sausage with beer form the _ goûter _ usually take at five or six o'clock and at nine follow a supper as solid as the dinner the german be not lounger as the french and italian who for the most part spend all they spare time in coffee-house when i mention to a bavarian that i could find no _ cafés _ in munich resemble those in france and italy he say with emphasis _ gott bewahre _ -lrb- god forbid -rrb- i could not help think he be in the right for those splendid _ cafés _ be very seduce to young people and tend to encourage a life of idleness and to keep they from they study the lower _ bourgeoisie _ and _ stubenmädchen _ -lrb- _ maidservant _ -rrb- wear a singular head dress it be make of stuff work with silver or gold and resemble two horn stick out one at each ear this head dress must be costly this class of woman wear also on _ fête _ day gold cross collar and earring the bavarian seem a frank honest set of people tho ' sometimes a little rough in they exterior deportment the character of otto of wittelsbach in the tragedy of that name give the best idea of the bavarian character i have make acquaintance here with a mr f ----- a austrian gentleman and two polish gentleman the one a officer and the other a medical man they be brother and have both serve in the french army we have agree to travel to vienna together on board of the raft which start every week from munich to vienna this raft bring to every day between twelve o'clock and two near some town or village on the bank of the river in order to allow the passenger to dine and anchor every evening at seven o'clock near some town or village to sup and sleep you have only to tell the _ flossmeister _ or master of the raft at what inn you mean to put up or if you have no preference he will recommend you one and at five the next morning he go he round to the different inn to collect he passenger and at six get under weigh vienna 2nd August i leave munich on the 25th July and arrive on the 6th day of we journey 30th July at vienna the _ floss _ or raft on board of which we embark be about as long as the main deck of a eighty-four gun ship and about forty foot in breadth it be construct of strong spar lash together on the spar be construct a large platform and on the platform several cabin contain table and chair mr f -- the pole and myself hire a cabin to ourselves on the raft be a great deal of merchandize go to vienna at vienna the _ flossmeister _ after land he passenger and merchandize sell he raft and return on horseback to munich a raft be construct weekly at munich from wood fell in the tyrol and float on the isar down to munich we arrive the first evening at freysingen but it be nearly dark when we arrive it seem however as far as we could observe to be a neat village at any rate we meet with a very comfortable inn there with good fare and good bed we meet with a very pleasant family on board the raft bind to landshut m and mme s be extremely well-informed people and they two daughter very fine girl we arrive the following day at twelve o'clock at landshut which be a very fine town there be a immense gothic tower or steeple to the church of st martin about 450 foot in height at deckendorf where the isar flow into the danube i salute for the first time that noble river we stop the night at pillshofen and arrive the following day at twelve o'clock at passau passau be a large well build and handsome city and be situate on the confluent of three river the inn the illst and the danube for here the two former flow into the latter one on each side each of these river just before the point of juncture seem to be of different color for example the danube appear blue the inn white and the illst black at passau we put up at the wild man -lrb- _ zum wilden mann _ -rrb- a favorite sign for inn in these part the cathedral and _ residenz-schloss _ be striking building and the city have a lively and grand appearance the woman appear to be in general handsome and well dress we bring to the evening at engelhardtzell where the barrier paint black and yellow announce we return to the austrian territory we undergo at the custom house a rigid search for tobacco : they even take away the tobacco that some passenger have in they pouch they be likewise very rigid about we passport the english passport do not please they at all on account of the feature of the bearer not be specify therein and as i answer they question in german they suppose I to be a native of that country and ask I what business i have with a british passport i reply : _ weil ich ein engländer bin -- sie ein engländer sie ` sind gewiss aus nord deutschland sie sprechen recht gut deutsch -- meine herren ich bin ein engländer : viele engländer studieren und sprechen deutsch und wenn sièmit mir eine langeunterredung gehalten hätten so hätten sie bald ausgefunden durch meine sprachfehler dass ich kein geborner deutscher bin -- aber sie haben unsere fragen vollkomman gut beantwortet -- warum nicht man hat mir die nehmlichen fragen so wiederholten malen gestellt dass ich die dazu gehörigen antworte auswendig habe wie em katechismus _ -lrb- 123 -rrb- the officer laugh take up a pen _ viséd _ and give I back my passport the whole of the country on the bank of this noble river the danube be picturesque and present much variety there can not be a more delightful summer tour than a descent down this river the next town of consequence that we arrive at be linz a large populous and beautifully build city and capital of upper austrium the circumjacent country be in part mountainous the danube be very broad here and there be a immensely long wooden bridge we put up at the inn _ zum goldenen kreutz _ -lrb- golden cross -rrb- here it become indispensably necessary to change we money for austrian paper for that sort of it call _ wiener währung _ -lrb- vienna security -rrb- since neither foreign coin nor another description of austrian paper call _ conventions-münze _ -lrb- conventional currency -rrb- be current for ordinary purpose and it be necessary to get they change for the current paper _ wiener währung_to explain this matter more fully and clearly : there be two sort of paper money in the austrian dominion one be call _ conventions-münze _ -lrb- conventional currency -rrb- which be fully equivalent to gold and sliver and can not be refuse as such throughout the whole of the austrian dominion the other call _ wiener währung _ -lrb- vienna security -rrb- be current and payable in austrium proper only and bear a loss out of the archduchy the value of the _ wiener währung _ fluctuate considerably but the usual par of exchange be as 2 to 1 : that mean two hundred florin _ wiener währung _ be equal to one hundred _ convenzions-münze _ or gold and silver money even the _ convenzions-münze _ bear a loss tho ' trifle out of the imperial dominion the exchange have be know to have be at 400 per cent that be four hundred florin _ wiener währung _ be only worth one hundred florin gold and silver but just now it may be reckon a little beyond par fluctuate from 200 to 220 in fact the value of a florin _ wiener währung _ may be calculate at a frank in french money all this be exceedingly troublesome to traveller particularly to those who do not understand the german language for as they can not read the inscription it would be difficult for they to know the difference between one sort of paper money and the other and they might be seriously impose upon i advise therefore all traveller before they arrive at the austrian frontier whether come from bavarium saxony or italy to buy up the _ wiener währung _ note they may meet with and which may be purchase at great profit probably beyond the frontier whereas if they defer purchase till they arrive within the austrian frontier they can only procure the _ wiener währung _ at the common rate of exchange current at linz we find ourselves again in a wine country linz be renown for the beauty of its woman and we have a most favorable specimen in we landlord 's daughter one of the most beautiful girl i ever behold we talk to she a great deal and a scene ridiculous enough occur she have very beautiful arm which we all seem to admire and all at once by instinct as it be the two pole lift up one arm and i the other and we respective lip be fasten on either arm at the same moment as if by word of command we apologize for the liberty we take say that she arm be perfectly irresistible and that we have never see such fine one before she accept we excuse with the utmost good nature and laugh very heartily she father be a man of information and a good classical scholar a thing which be by no means uncommon among the inn-keeper of germany we stop here that night and the ensue forenoon we have a excellent supper very good wine and we drink to the health of the fair amalium the host 's daughter we host who be a friend of mr f -- 's give we the best of every thing and we expence do not amount to more than seven florin _ wiener währung _ for supper bed breakfast and dinner we pass the forenoon in visit the different part of the city and we be strike with the appearance of opulence and industry that prevail before we arrive at mölk which be the next important place we pass the town of en and beyond that the famous _ strudel _ or whirlpool which be dangerous at time for boat we raft be completely whirl round this whirlpool be cause by rock rise abruptly out of the water the popular tradition be that this whirlpool be the abode of a very malicious and spiteful _ wassernixe _ undine or water goblin who delight in drown passenger the scenery hereabouts be more wild and romantic than what we have hitherto pass and bear a great resemblance to the landscape on the rhine between mayence and coblentz mölk be a abbey and a very magnificent edifice it be situate on a eminence which form the angle with the river and rise quite _ à pio _ from the water 's edge it lie quite _ en face _ to those who approach it descend the stream so that the river seem to be terminate by it it command a noble prospect i have only time to inspect hastily the church beyond mölk be a range of rock that bear a great resemblance to a wall and jut out a great deal towards the river it be call the _ devil 's wall _ from the tradition of the devil have endeavor to make a wall to dam up the river above this wall be the famous castle and vineyard call _ spitz be platz _ and further on be the castle of dierenstein situate on a mountain on the left bank of the danube the ascent be very steep this castle now in ruin be the place where richard coeur de lion be confine the wall only of the castle and part of the chapel be all that remain we do not fail to visit a place of such celebrity a convent lie below it we bring to the night at a large village where there be a excellent inn and the next day the leopoldsberg burst forth to view announce to we the approach to vienna we anchor at nussdorf where there be a custom house and from whence the distance to vienna be about one and half mile english after have my trunk examine i hire a hackney coach and drive into vienna the barrier beyond the suburb be call _ line _ and between the suburb and the old town be a esplanade we enter the suburb by the _ währinger linie _ and the old town by the _ rothe thor _ -lrb- red gate -rrb- and from thence i repair to the inn _ zum weissen wolf _ -lrb- white wolf -rrb- in the _ altem fleischmarkt _ -lrb- old meat-market -rrb- vienna augt 4 the old town of vienna be not very large since you can walk round its circumference on the rampart in two hour it be formerly fortify but the french blow up the fortification leave only the rampart and by so do they do a thing of great utility for the viennese and give to the austrian government a excellent opportunity of join the old town to the magnificent faubourg by fill up the esplanade which separate they with street and square which would prevent the unpleasant effect of dust in dry and the mud in wet weather for this dust and mud render the esplanade almost at all time a disagreeable promenade there be a sharp wind prevalent almost the whole year at vienna which blow about the dust _ en tourbillon _ here then be a excellent opportunity afford by the blow up of the fortification of pave the whole of the esplanade and fill it up with street but no the austrian government seem determine upon restore the fortification and a considerable number of workman be employ this be very silly for these fortification be not of the least use against a foreign enemy inasmuch as the enemy can always erect he battery among the faubourg and need only make one parallel the protection and cover afford to he by the faubourg render the other two superfluous the faubourg be by far the finest part of the city and the garrison of the old town in endeavor to defend it would destroy by every shot they should fire the fine building on the faubourg of the folly of make such a defense they be make fully sensible in 1809 one of the archduke throw himself into the old town of vienna with a intention of defend it to the last and refuse to surrender napoleon cause battery to be erect on the _ rennweg _ or _ corso _ cover by the church of st charle the manege and palace of the hungarian noble guard all magnificent building in the faubourg he then summon the garrison of the old town again to surrender say : every shot fire against the besieger destroy you own most valuable property and finest edifice this argument back by the entreaty of the citizen have its effect and the capitulation be sign this show the perfect inutility of fortify the old town of vienna against a foreign enemy indeed a capital city should never be fortify it generally contain too many thing of value ever to be expose to the risk of a bombardment it would seem however that the object of the austrian government in reconstruct these work be to keep its own subject at vienna in check but in this case it would be much more advisable to construct a fortress on the height of kahlenberg or of leopoldsberg both of which command the city and the whole expanse below the turk be encamp on the kahlenberg at the famous siege of vienna vienna proper the old town be a gothic city but a very handsome one the street be in general broad and well paved but the _ place _ or square be small with the exception of the _ herrengasse _ where the nobility reside the rest of vienna be inhabit by shopkeeper and wholesale dealer and the shop be brilliant and well fit up the _ kärnthner strasse _ a long and tolerably broad street and the _ kohlmarkt _ present the greatest display of wealth indeed the _ kärnthner strasse _ may be consider as the principal street this street and the _ kohlmarkt _ have a great resemblance to the finest part of holborn the _ graben _ also present a fine display of shop and may be term the bond street of vienna the _ sanct stephan platz _ where the cathedral church of vienna call _ st stephan kirche _ stand be the largest _ place _ in vienna the cathedral be a very ancient and curious gothic edifice and the steeple be nearly 450 foot high i happen to enter the cathedral one day on the occasion of a solemn requiem celebrate for the soul of prince metternich 's father have it be for the son instead of the father many a honorable man persecute at the instigation of that most machiavelic of all minister might exclaim in make a slight alteration in a well know epitaph : cy-gît m -- ah qu'il est bien pour son repo et pour le mien among the other striking building in the old town be the _ hofburg _ or imperial palace a very extensive quadrangular building with a large court in its center a guard mount here every day at eleven o'clock it be in one of the saloon of this palace that the celebrated congress of vienna be hold a congress whose labor will be long and severely feel by europe and duly appreciate by posterity who will feel any other sentiment but that of gratitude for the arrangement enter into there the _ hofburg _ be build by leopold vii in 1200 this building from its be extremely irregular and from its have receive addition at interval in the different style of architecture have be aptly enough consider as the type of the austrian monarchy and of its growth from a markgraviate to a empire in _ this _ by the continued acquisition of foreign territory differ from each other in manners and hi speech in _ that _ by the continue addition of various specimen of architecture and style of building in its augmentation vienna aug 8th i be very well content with my abode at the _ weisser wolf _ tho ' it be not a first-rate hotel they be very civil people and i have a excellent and spacious room for two florin _ wiener whärung _ per diem lodgings be the only thing that be dear in vienna every other article be however cheaper than in any other city i have yet be in all kind of hungarian wine may be have at the most reasonable price i generally breakfast at a neighbouring _ café _ in the _ fleischmarkt _ for the sake of read the _ allgemeine zeitung _ which be take in there and which be the only journal have a shade of liberality which be permit in the austrian dominion from the hour of twelve to three dinner _ à la carte _ be serve at the _ weisser wolf _ for two and half florin _ ww _ i get a excellent dinner with a bottle of offener wine the wine of offen resemble much that of bordeaux in its quality and flavor the tariff however of the dinner and wine vary daily a few kreutzer in consequence of the eternal fluctuation of the _ ww _ so that every morning a fresh tariff be affix to the wainscot of the saloon where the dinner be serve supper serve likewise _ à la carte _ be at its full tide between the hour of eight and ten o'clock and as vienna be renown for the celebrity of its beefsteak and cutlet call here _ rostbraten _ these and a salad seem to be the favorite dish for supper my morning i have hitherto pass in lounge about the _ kärnthner gasse st stephen 's platz kohlmarkt _ etc for a hour before dinner the fashionable promenade be on the rampart in front of the palace of duke albert of saxe-teschen in the evening on the _ prater _ in a carriage on horseback or on foot the _ prater _ be of immense extent and offer a great variety of amusement and sight i generally return home at night pretty well fatigue from my ramble there be another great inconvenience at vienna result from the fluctuation of the current money and this be that a stranger dwelling at a inn be sure to be disturbed five or six time in the morning sometimes as early as five or six o'clock by jew who rap at he door to enquire if he want to exchange gold and silver against currency or _ vice versâ _ i use to lose all patience at be so disturbed in the morning and be oblige in self-defence to put a affiche on the door of my room to this effect : _ man kauft und verkauft hier nicht kein wechsler darf hereintreten _ here there be no buying and sell no money changer be allow to come in and i hereby recommend to all stranger not to treat with these jew but on they arrival or at any time they think fit to go to a banking establishment in this city where every day after eleven o'clock you can exchange you gold and silver for paper at the just rate of exchange as publish at the bourse pay only a very slight premium and on leave vienna to go to the same establishment to change you superfluous _ wiener währung _ for _ convenzion münze _ or gold and silver money for when the jew tell you the rate of exchange be so and so you conclude probably you bargain with they and on enquire at the bourse you find that the jew have make a percentage of six or eight per cent out of you _ loui d'or _ be the best foreign coin to bring into the austrian dominion next to they in utility be the dutch ducat or _ geharnischte männer _ as they be term from the figure of the man in armor upon they all other corn suffer a loss in proportion the banker in vienna pay the foreign bill of exchange in _ convenzion münze _ which you must afterwards change for _ wiener währung _ the only current money in vienna and austrium but what make it additionally troublesome be that here in vienna there be particular payment which must absolutely be pay in gold or silver or _ convenzion münze _ and _ not wiener währung _ for instance the franking of foreign letter at the post office where they do not take the _ wiener währung _ in vain you may intreat they to take the _ wiener währung _ at any rate they please no you must go elsewhere and buy from the first person you can meet with as much gold and silver as be require for the franking of the letter so bigott be they in the austrian dominion to the letter of the law this happen to I : i want to frank three letter for england and i go to the post office with _ wiener währung _ paper not be aware of this regulation and i be oblige to return to my hotel to lay hold of a jew and to buy from he as much gold and silver as be requisite for the franking of the letter at the _ wechselbank _ or bank of exchange i have before mention the crowd that attend daily be immense but the business be carry on without hurry or confusion you hand in you paper or you gold and silver coin the clerk who receive it give you a order on paper for the amount specify which paper you take into another room and therein receive the amount this establishment however remain open only two hour every day between eleven and one i believe so if you be too late for this interval of time you must apply to the broker christian or israelite vienna August 11th we leave the old town by the _ burg-thor _ and cross the esplanade direct we course to the _ rennweg _ one of the suburb in order to view the majestic edifice of st charle which be equal in the beauty of its architecture to many of the finest church in rome its façade and cupola render it one of the most striking building belong to vienna we next visit the _ manège _ and the palace call the palace of the hungarian noble guard they be both beautiful edifice the faubourg of vienna be build in the modern style and they building both public and private excellent in they way and in the best state the street of the faubourg be broad but not pave the most celebrated of these faubourg be _ marium hülf _ _ leopold-stadt _ _ landstrasse _ the _ rennweg _ the _ wühringer gasse _ and i be persuade that if the old town be unite to the faubourg by means of street and square and the esplanade fill up with building vienna would perhaps be the handsomest city in europe and the fourth in size for the best building and palace be in the faubourg viz the military college the polytechnic school st charle ' church the porcelain fabric the palace of esterhazy kaunitz stahremberg schwarzenberg palfy and the beautiful palace and ground of belvedere in which last be a noble collection of picture open to the every branch of science be on the grandest scale after dinner we repair to the _ prater _ cross a branch of the danube which here form several island the _ prater _ require and deserve particular mention part of it be something in the style of the _ champ elysées _ at pari and it be fully equal to it in the variety of amusement and enjoyment to be meet with there but it be far larger and more beautiful on account of its landscape and the diversified manner in which the grounds be lay out the _ prater _ then be a immense park lay out on a island of considerable extent on the danube the nearest faubourg to it be the _ leopoldstadt _ which be also the most fashionable one and a bridge conduct you from that faubourg direct into the _ prater _ the _ prater _ present a mixture of garden meadow upland and forest the lofty tree arrange in avenue or in clump give a delightful protect shade on the road destine for the carriage there be every afternoon a most brilliant display of carriage another avenue be destine for equestrian and two avenue one on each side of these two for pedestrian there be besides wind footpath that conduct you all over this vast extent of ground and circular grass plot surround by tree where the pedestrian may repose and eat and drink if he will here be _ restaurant _ in plenty _ cafés _ panorama exhibition of wild beast swing tennis court place for run at the ring do for burlesque dramatic performance _ farceur _ juggler de bach 's equestrian amphitheatre in the style of franconus _ salle de danse _ bath billiard room gaming table and even house appropriate to gallantry in fact the _ prater _ be quite the paradise of the bourgeoisie of vienna who be fond of the pleasure of the table and take every opportunity of make dinner and supper party the bourgeois of vienna be far more sensual than spiritual and not at all disposed to self-denial excellent ham and sausage be to be have here and the viennese who dine and sup heartily at he own house never fail during he evening promenade to take a tolerable good portion of ham or sausage with a proportion of offen wine or maylander beer by way of stay he stomach during the tedious interval between dinner and supper i need scarce add that smoking be universal as indeed it be all over germany for i scarcely ever see a german without a pipe either in he mouth or fasten to he coat and a bag or pouch of tobacco either in he pocket or attach to he button hole in the _ prater _ dance often take place in the open air between the grisette of vienna who be in general handsome and well make and who dress well and they lover and admirer the _ prater _ be first open to the public by the emperor joseph ii the _ au-garten _ be another place of recreation and amusement but on a smaller and much more tranquil and sober scale than the _ prater _ none of the lower class think of come here tho ' it be open to every body decently dress : there be not that profuse eating and drinking go forward it be more properly speak a promenade and form a garden with alley of tree where music be often perform and there be a superb saloon where refreshment may be have the _ au-garten _ be frequent chiefly by the _ noblesse _ and _ haute bourgeoisie _ in the morning likewise it be a fashionable resort to drink the mineral water it adjoin the _ prater _ be on the same island it be the favorite lounge of joseph ii who open it to the public by affix this inscription on one of the gate : allen menschen gewidmete erlustigung von ihrem schätzer place of recreation open to all man by they esteemer vienna aug 13th there be a great number of theater at vienna two be situate in the old town viz the _ hof-theater _ and the _ burg-theater _ the _ hof-theater _ be only open when the court be at vienna and they be now at baden ten league distant the _ burg-theater _ be open all the year round and may be consider as the national theater it be much frequent by the bourgeoisie and inhabitant of the old town who do not chuse to take the trouble to go to the _ wieden-theater _ which be situate in the faubourg and which be more of a classical and fashionable theater than the other inasmuch as it be more elegantly and classically build better fit up and have a far better company of comedian at the _ burgtheater _ i see kotzebue 's _ edelsinn und armuth _ perform the wieden theater which be as i have say in the faubourg be the handsomest theater perhaps in europe for its size it be not large but it be fit up with so much taste and you see and hear so well every ornament be so chaste and there be nothing at all tawdry or superfluous it be i really think a model of what every theater ought to be there be a good deal of bronze about it which give it a classical appearance and the box be support by caryatide in bronze there be a peculiarity in all the theater at vienna which be that in the _ parterre _ you must sit in the place the number of which be mark on you ticket these place be call _ gesperrte sitze _ and each seat resemble a armchair when not occupy the seat be fold up and lock to the back of the chair until the person who hold the ticket correspond to its number come to take it so that no other but the person hold the ticket correspond to the number can take it and you be thus never likely to be shove out of you place as you be at most of the theater in europe there be man station at the door who follow you into the _ parterre _ to unlock and let down a seat for you and to they you give you ticket with a slight gratification which be however quite optional you ticket you previously pay for at the door vienna augt 20th i have be to see schönbrunn the usual residence of the young napoleon but he be now at baden with the imperial family where he mother who be always a object of suspicion and espionnage _ journey to prague _ i leave vienna on the 28th August in a _ landkutsche _ and arrive at prague on the first of September these _ landkutsche _ be on the same plan and footing with the _ vetture _ in italy and travel in the same manner with this difference however that the _ landkutscher _ do not usually as the _ vetturinus _ do undertake to provide for the supper and bed of they passenger in a word you be not _ spesato _ and in germany there be not the least necessity for it for there be no such thing as extortion on the part of the german innkeeper who be by far the most respectable of that profession besides in most place everything be _ tariffed _ and where it be not the landlord never make a unreasonable demand or attempt to make foreigner pay more than native whereas in italy if you be not _ spesato _ there be no bound to the rapacity of the innkeeper witness mine host of terracina both italy and germany present the greatest convenience for traveller as the _ landkutsche _ or _ vetture _ be continually pass from town to town there be however this difference between they that the italian _ vetturinus _ will abate they price if they carriage be full except one place and that they must start whereas the german _ landkutscher _ never abate they price i pay for my journey from vienna to prague thirty-five florin _ wiener währung _ and we make the journey in five day we first day 's journey bring we to höllabrunn have stoppd to dinner at stockeran the road be excellent and the several town and village we past faubourg the street be broader and it have a more cheerful and less confine appearance than the old town of vienna the position of prague too be very romantic and picturesque part of it lie on a mountain and part on a plain and it stand on the confluent of two river the mulda and the braun the upper part of the city call oberburg stand on a height call ratschin and on this height stand a most magnificent palace and other stately building there be a beautiful panoramic view from this part of prague in this part of the city too be the cathedral of st wenzel or wenceslaus who be its founder he tomb and that of st john nepomucene a favorite saint of the bohemian be in this church the cathedral be of extreme solidity but little ornamented have be plunder by the swede in 1648 the canopy over the shrine of st john nepomucene have a profusion of votive offering append to it the lower part of prague be divide into two part by the mulda the bridge across the mulda be one of the finest in europe it have twenty-four arch its length be 1700 foot and its breadth 35 among several statue on this bridge be a very remarkable one of jesus christ make of bronze gilt which cost a large sum of money to its founder a jew there be a latin inscription on it which explain the paradox there stand on the same spot a wooden statue of christ in the xvi century one day a opulent jew on pass by make some scoffing or contemptuous remark on it he be overhear by some of the people accuse of blasphemy and condemn to die but on express great contrition and offer to pay a fine to any amount he be pardon on the condition of he promise to erect a bronze statue gilt of jesus christ on the same spot at he own expense with a inscription explain the reason of its construction which promise he punctually perform prague abound in jew two-third at least of its population be of that persuasion in the lower town the most striking edifice be the palace of the wallenstein family descendant of the famous wallenstein so distinguish in the thirty year war annex to this palace be a spacious garden which be open to the public as a promenade it be well lay out there be a large aviary this palace cover a vast extent of ground the colloredo family who be descend from wenceslaus have a superb palace in this city and there be a stable belong to it partly in marble and of rich architecture capable of contain thirty-six horse no traveller who come to prague should omit visit these two palace of wallenstein and colloredo on the bridge over the mulda before mention be the statue in bronze of st john nepomucene on the spot from whence he be throw into the river by he brother saint king wenceslaus for refuse to divulge the gallantry of he -lrb- wenceslaus ' -rrb- wife to whom he be confessor a prague who be renown for they beauty and complaisance the jewish bury ground be a curiosity for a person who have never visit the oriental country the tombstone be stow thick together everybody shall start for dresden the diligence go off only once a week but i have engage a car or rather light basket waggon draw by two horse -lrb- a vehicle very common in germany -rrb- to convey I to dresden in two day and half i be to pay for half of the waggon and another traveller will pay for the remain half before i leave prague i must tell you that i have find out the origin of the german phrase _ jemand den korb zu geben -lrb- to give the basket -rrb- _ which mean a refusal of marriage thus when a young lady refuse a offer of marriage on the part of she admirer the phrase be : _ sie hat ihm den korb gegeben _ -lrb- _ she have give he the basket _ -rrb- hitherto i have not meet with any one who could explain to I satisfactorily the origin of so singular a phrase but on read lately a volume of the _ volksmährchen _ -lrb- _ popular tale _ -rrb- i find not only the derivation of this phrase but also that of the name of the city of prague both be connect in the same story and both concern the history of prague the story be as follow libussa duchess of bohemia have three lover two of whom be not remarkably intelligent but the third possess a great deal of talent and be she favorite she be much importune by the rival suitor she appear before they one day with a basket fill with plum in she hand and say she would give she hand in marriage to whoever of they should guess the follow arithmetical riddle she say : one of you shall take half the plum that be in this basket and one over : another shall take half of what remain and one over : the third shall take half of what still remain and three over and then all the plum will have be take now tell I how many plum there be in the basket she favorite be the only one who could guess the number of plum which be _ thirty _ to he therefore she give she hand and the plum and to the other suitor the empty basket hence the phrase the solution of the question be as follow : a take half of the plum in the basket -lrb- 30 -rrb- and one over 15 + 1 = 16 b half of what remain -lrb- 14 -rrb- and one over 7 + 1 = 8 c half of what remain -lrb- 6 -rrb- and three over 3 + 3 = 6 -- total 30 now with regard to the origin of the city of prague the former residence be much too small and libussa direct she workman to build a town on the spot where they should find at midday a man make the _ best use of he tooth _ they begin they research and one day at that hour discover a carpenter saw a block of wood it strike they that this laborious man be make a better use of he tooth -lrb- viz tooth of he saw -rrb- than the mere feeder and they judge that this ought to be the place where the town should be build they therefore proceed to trace with a plough the circumference of the town on ask the carpenter what he be about to make with the block he be saw he say a threshold for a door which be call _ prah _ or _ praha _ in the bohemian language and libussa give to the city the name of _ praha _ or _ prag _ berlin 24th sept berlin have a splendid and cheerful appearance with fine broad street superb white building and palace for the most part in the grecian taste it have quite the appearance in short of a italian city nearly all the street be at right angle they be keep very clean and the shop make a brilliant display i feel so much pain in my leg from the effect of my pedestrian journey that i be sort usually drunk here be the medoc the price of article of prune necessity be dearer in berlin than either at dresden or vienna particularly the article of wash which be dearer than in any country i have yet visit the next morning i begin my ramble and direct my course to the favorite and fashionable promenade of the _ beau monde _ at all hour of the day i mean in the fine street or alley _ unter difficult to excite a revolt the various german government be carry on very paternally and the government be scarcely feel habit of obedience have take deep root among the people and a german peasant as long as he get enough to eat and drink do not conceive himself unhappy or think of a change i could not help laugh the other day at a little village near berlin when i hear some peasant talk of
