why do he leave elba he have surely plenty to eat and drink -rrb- this good peasant could not conceive that a man bless with these comfort should like to change he situation or run any risk to do so french as well as german be commonly speak in berlin and i be glad to see that the prejudice against the french be wear off if the french and prussian could understand one another and know they own interest or if the french have a liberal national government i mean one more identify with the interest of the people than the present one be what advantage might not rise therefrom they be natural ally and unite they might be able effectually to humble the overbearing insolence and political coxcombry of the czar shake to its center the systematic despotism and light-fearing leader of austrium and keep in check the commercial greediness monopolize spirit and tory arrogance of england the german political writer duly appreciate the illiberal policy of england towards the continental nation by which she invariably help to crush liberty on the continent in the hope of paralyse they energy and industry in order to compel they to buy english manufacture and in fine to make they dependent on england for every article of consumption england ever since the beginning of the reign of george iii to the present day have be always ready to lend a hand to crush liberty to perpetuate abuse and to rivet the fetter of monarchial feudal and ecclesiastical tyranny these be fact and can not be deny the english people have be tax to the last farthing to support a war of privilege against freedom and europe be in consequence prostrate at the foot of a unprincipled coalition thro ' england 's arm and england 's gold and then a english minister and he vile hireling journal tell you that the continental nation be not ripe for and do not deserve liberty even the pope and grand turk both so much dread by we pious ancestor have be support caress and subsidize in order to help to put down all effort make to obtain rational liberty which the courtier always affect to stigmatize with the name of jacobinism while a number of needy individual have enrich themselves by the public plunder and byaiding and abet the system all _ novus homine _ man who have there be more to gain on the other side than by espouse toryism would not have be backward man who be jacobin in the real sense of the word however they cloak themselves under the specious name of church and king man upholder of pitt and he system for which they affect a veneration they be far from really feel man in fact whose political scruple of whatever nature they be would soon melt away dresden 5th October i have be fortunate in get into very comfortable lodgings have two room and as much firing as i chuse for eight _ request the indulgence of exercise they religion publicly and the grant it have produce no evil consequence liberalism and the most unreserved toleration in matter of religion be the order of the day extent and beautifully lay out but a number of fine tree have be knock down and mutilate by cannon shot during the battle of dresden in 1818 when this garden be occupy by the ally troops and expose to a heavy fire of fifty piece of cannon from a battery erect by napoleon on the opposite side of the river which completely command and enfilade the whole range of the garden how the palace itself escape be knock to piece be wonderful but i suppose napoleon must have give order to spare it as much as possible this palace be of beautiful structure and in the style of a italian villa statue of the twelve caesar and bas-relief adorn the exterior the column and pilaster be of the corinthian order as for the interior it be unfurnished and have be so since the seven year ' war when it be thereby during the battle of dresden the slaughter in this garden be immense and the ally be finally drive out of it the gardener related to I a affect story of a young lady of dresden whose lover be berlin with the idea of pass the winter there and of proceed in the summer to moscow thro ' the interest of my friend col d ------ and baron de f ------ i have be ballot for and admit a member of a club or society here call the _ ressource _ it be hold in a large house on the _ markt platz _ and be indeed a most agreeable resource to all foreigner for ` tis in this society that they be likely to meet and form acquaintance with the _ noblesse _ principal _ bourgeoisie _ and _ litteratus _ it be conduct on the most liberal scale and not confine to those of birth and fortune good character polite behavior and litterary requirement will ensure admittance to a candidate this society consist of member and honorary member among the honorary member be foreigner and other whose stay in dresden be short but whoever remain for more than one year must cease to be a honorary member and must be ballot for in order to become a permanent member and should he be blackball he cease to belong to the society altogether this be a very good regulation a year be a sufficient time of proof for the character and conduct of a person and should he during this interval prove himself obnoxious to the member of the society they can at its expiration exclude he for ever afterwards no enquiry be make as to the character and conduct of a person who be admit as a honorary member : it be sufficient that he be recommend by a permanent member which be deem a sufficient guarantee for he respectability in this society there be dine room billiard room card room a large reading room here too be a to they family after a introduction you may go at any hour of the evening you please : but morning visit be not much in fashion since the _ toilette _ be seldom make till after dinner which be always early in germany there be no get dinner after three o'clock in any part of dresden besides the _ ressource _ there be several other club here such as the _ harmonic _ and other the public ball be give at the _ hôtel de pologne _ twice a week viz one for the _ noblesse _ and one for the _ bourgeoisie _ none of the female _ bourgeoisie _ be admit to the ball and society of the _ noblesse _ and only such of the male as occupy post or employment at court or under government such as _ königs-rath _ _ hof-rath _ or officer of the army it be therefore usual when the sovereign wish to introduce a person of merit among the _ bourgeoisie _ into the upper circle that he give he the title of _ rath _ or counsellor but this priviledge of be presentable at court do not extend to they wife and daughter all the military officer from whatever class of life they spring have introduction _ de jure _ into the ball and society of the _ noblesse _ and be always in uniform but when they attend the ball of the _ bourgeoisie _ it be the etiquette for they to wear plain clothes : at the ball of the _ bourgeoisie _ therefore not a uniform be to be see i observe by far the prettiest woman at the class be extremely well educate most of they be proficient in music and be verse in french and italian litterature they seem amiable and goodnatured and by no means _ minaudières _ as lady mary wortley montague have rather unjustly term they for they appear to I to be the most frank artless creature i ever behold and to have no sort of _ minauderie _ or _ coquetterie _ about they beauty be the appanage of the saxon woman hence the proverb in rhyme : darauf bin ich gegangen nach sachsen will die schönen mädchen auf den baümen wachsen in english : behold I land now on saxon ground where lovely damsel on the tree be find a taste for litterature be indeed general throughout the whole nation and this city be consider as the athen of germany dresden nov 8th i have be at the theater and learning force into the service he prove nothing and this very man be probably ignorant in the extreme of modern political history and that of he own time and have more pedantry than taste such a man the people which can only be thoroughly learn by read popular author in they original language : for there be several author of the merit of whose style it be impossible to form a adequate idea in a the defunct these chorister be all dress in black and they style of singing be melodious solemn and impressive smoking be so prevalent here and in all part of germany that if you wish to denote one of the male sex _ smoker _ would be quite a synonymous word such be the passion for this enjoyment that even at the ball the young man the moment they have finish the waltz quit the hand of they partner and rush into another room in order to smoke nor would the beauty of venus nor the wit of minerva be powerful enough to restrain the young german from give way to he darling practice smoking tobacco have i think this visible effect that it serve to calm all tumultuous passion and what confirm I in this idea be that most young german in commence life as adult be full of enthusiastic and even exaggerated notion of liberty and equality they be romantic to a degree that be difficult to be conceive and seem to be restrain by no selfish or worldly idea this you would suppose would tend to render they rather turbulent subject under a autocratical government but all this _ schwärmerey _ evaporate literally in smoke : they take to they pipe and by degree the fume of tobacco cause all these lofty idea to dissipate : the pipe become more and more necessary to they existence and console they for they wrong real or imaginary and in three or four year they sit down contentedly to they several occupation as strait-forward painstaking plodding man quite satisfied to follow the routine chalk out for they and either totally forget all ambitious view or become too indolent to make any sacrifice to obtain they and this _ virtue come from tobacco _ the german hippogriff become a ox dull and domestic and tread out the corn place before he content to have he share thereof in peace and quietness the german government which be mild and paternal be fully aware of this and allow the utmost liberty of speech well know that thanks to that friend and ally of legitimacy tobacco the romantic visionary and somewhat refractory youth will subside into a tranquil _ ganz alltäglicher mann _ and become totally averse to any innovation which demand the sacrifice of repose the pipe which have this sedative effect on political effervescence have a still stronger similar effect it be say on the passion of love hence the german husband be proverbially sluggish but the lady none of whom smoke preserve they romanticity during they whole life and would if they have they choice give they hand to foreigner who be more attentive to they than they own countryman the young lady here be ` tis say extremely romantic in they idea of love and capable of the strongest attachment they think that any thing should be pardon to sincere passion it have be relate to I that some time ago a young man who be devotedly attach to a girl on the father refuse he consent to the marriage stab the girl and then himself a immense number of young lady attend they funeral to throw flower over the grave of the two lover assuredly the young man be only a noviciate in smoking everybody must i think admire the saxon woman they be in general handsome and have fine shape they be warm hearted and affectionate and they be almost universally well educate indeed the whole saxon people be so amiable that foreigner find themselves so happy here that they be unwilling to quit the country very many form matrimonial attachment in short this people fully merit the epithet a celebrated english traveller -lrb- sherlock -rrb- -lrb- 127 -rrb- have bestow on they when he call they a _ herrlich volk _ dresden jan 8d 1819 i have make a excursion to meissen which lie on the same bank of the river with the old town of dresden at a distance of twelve mile as there be no road on the left bank of the river to meissen you must cross the river twice to arrive at it viz once at neustadt and once at meissen the road be on the right bank i put up at the _ hirsch _ -lrb- stag -rrb- a very comfortable inn i go to meissen with a view of see the russian contingent pass the elbe on they return from france which have be evacuate in consequence of the arrangement at aix-la-chapelle they appear a fine body of man clothe _ à la française _ and seem in high spirit they seem to have imbibe liberal idea during they residence in france for some of the officer who dine at the inn at meissen speak very comrade and friend and potent libation of _ doppel bier _ will no doubt be make meissen be say to be famous for the beauty of its woman and the few that i saw in the street do not contradict this reputation dresden jany 5th 1819 we have have several ball here waltz be the only sort of dance in fashion at dresden except now and then a polonaise i have witness a interesting spectacle in the _ grosser garten _ the pond or basin be completely freeze over and a russian prince gallitzin who be here have fit up a sort of _ montagne russ _ as they be call block of ice be place on a inclined garten _ with the _ beau monde _ every day from twelve to two o'clock so that you see we be in no want of amusement at dresden the king frequently attend the theater he be a tall fine look man and be _ shadow of justice _ could pretend to a indemnification at the expense of saxony in the year 1805 the king then elector of saxony strongly advise the prussian cabinet to forget its ancient rivalry here tho ' well versed and delighting in various branch of litterature can not overcome that strong national propensity to tale and romance wherein the _ terrific and supernatural _ abound in all they romance accordingly this taste prevail strongly nay even in some of the romance where the scene be lay in later time there be some such anachronism as the story of a spectre i recollect read a novel the scene of which be lay in italy about the time of the battle of marengo wherein a ghost be introduce who contribute mainly to the unravelling of the piece a young lady here of considerable talent and of general information confess to I when i ask she what subject pleased she most in the way of reading that nothing give she so much delight as _ geistergeschichten _ lewi ' romance of _ the monk _ be a great favorite in germany -lrb- 128 -rrb- by the bye he poetical tale of _ alonzo and imogen _ be evidently take from a similar subject in the _ volks-mährchen _ the weather have set in very cold and the elbe be nearly freeze over it be impossible to go out of the house without a _ pelz _ or cloak line with fur for otherwise on leave a room heat by a stove the effect of the cold be almost instantaneous and bring on a ague fit this i attribute to the excessive heat keep up in the room and house by the stove as smoking be so prevalent here this contribute much also to keep the body in a praeternatural heat and render it still more obnoxious to cold on removal from a room to the open air it have be remark by a medical author in the russian campaign in 1812 that the soldier of the southern nation and province viz provençaux gascon italian spaniard and portuguese endure the cold much better and suffer less from it than the german and hollander the reason be sufficiently obvious : the former live in the open air even in the middle of winter and seldom make use of a fire to warm themselves whereas the german and dutch live in a atmosphere of stove-heat and smoke and seldom like to stir abroad in the open air during winter unless necessity oblige they hence they become half-baked as it be they nerve be unstring they flesh flabby and they become so chilly as to suffer from the smallest exposure to the atmosphere in the house in germany on account of the stove the cold be never feel whereas it be very severely in italy and spain where many of the house have no fireplace on this account i prefer germany as a winter residence for i think there be no sensation so disagreeable as to feel cold in the house in the open air i do not care a fig for it for my cloak line with bearskin protect I amply the climate here in winter be a dry cold which be much more salubrious and agreeable to I than the changeable humid climate of great britain where though the cold be not so great it be much more severely feel -lrb- 126 -rrb- tacitus _ germanium _ c viii -- ed -lrb- 127 -rrb- martin sherlock -lrb- d 1797 -rrb- author of _ lettre d'un voyageur anglai _ which be publish in paris 1779 and the year after in london -lrb- 128 -rrb- matthew gregory lewi 1775-1818 publish _ ambrosio or the monk _ in 1795 -- ed chapter xviii march-april 1819 journey from dresden to leipzig -- the university of leipzig -- liberal spirit -- the english dislike in saxony -- the english government hostile to liberty -- journey to frankfort -- from frankfort to metz and pari -- af lemaître -- _ bon voyage _ to the ally -- return to england i leave dresden on the 2nd march 1819 a _ landkutsche _ convey I as far as leipzig in a day and half stop the first night at oschaly where there be a good inn at leipzig i put up at the _ hôtel de bavière _ and remain five day leipzig be a fine old gothic city it be as everybody know famous for its university and its fair which be hold twice a year in spring and in autumn and which be the greatest mart for book perhaps in the world the university of leipzig and indeed all the university of germany be in bad repute among the _ obscuranten _ and _ éteignoirs _ of the day on account of the liberal idea profess by the teacher and scholar in the university of leipzig every thing may be learn by those who chuse to apply but those who prefer remain idle may do so as there be less compulsion than at the english university there be however such a national enthusiasm for learn in all part of germany that the most careless and ill-disposed youth would never be about to support the ridicule of he fellow student be he backward in obtain prize but after all i have hear of the dissipation lawlessness and want of discipline at leipzig i can safely affirm that all these story be grossly exaggerated : and i fancy there be little other dissipation go forward than amours with _ stubenmädchen _ i do not hear of any drunkenness gaming or horse racing nor do the professor themselves who ought to be the best judge of what be go on complain of the insubordination of they pupil but what i principally admire in this and indeed in other german university be that there be no distinction of rank such as gold tassel etc no servile attention pay to sprig of nobility as in the university in england where the head of college and fellow be singularly condescend to the son of a peer a minister or a bishop perfect equality prevail in leipzig and the son of the proudest _ reichsgraf _ be allow no more priviledge than the son of a barber nor do the professor make the least difference between they in fact in spite of the vulgar belief in england respect the _ hauteur _ of the german _ noblesse _ and the vassalage of the other class i must say from experience that the german nobility show far less _ hauteur _ and have in general more really liberal idea than most part of we english aristocracy and a german burgher or shop-keeper would disdain to cringe before a nobleman as many shopkeeper aye and even gentry be sometimes know to do in england another circumstance too prove on how much more liberal a footing leipzig and other german university be than we english one which be that in england none but those who profess the religion of the church of england or conform to its ritual be admit but here all sect be tolerate and admit and all live in perfect harmony with each other the student be at liberty to chuse they place of worship and the sermon that be preach in the catholic as well as the protestant church be such as sensible man of whatever opinion might listen to with profit and without be shock by absurdity or intolerant idea mystery theologic sophistry and politics be carefully avoid and a pure morality a simple theosophy comprehensible to the meanest understanding pervade these simple discourse the consequence of this toleration and liberal spirit be that a union between the lutheran and calvinistic church have be effect i meet a number of mercantile people at the _ table d'hôte _ at leipzig in the _ hôtel de bavière _ and i enter a good deal into conversation with they but when they discover i be a englishman i could see a sudden coldness and restraint in they demeanor for we be very unpopular in germany owe to the conduct of we cabinet and they have a great distrust of we the saxon complain terribly of we government for sanction the dismemberment of they country and of the insolent letter of castlereagh it be singular enough that saxony be the only country where english goods be allow to be import free of duty but we great and good ally the king of prussium -lrb- as these goods must pass thro ' he territory -rrb- have impose a tolerably heavy transit duty i be glad of it this be as it should be i rejoice at any obstacle that be put to british commerce i rejoice when i hear of we merchant suffer and i quite delight to hear of a bankruptcy they the english merchant contribute with they gold to uphold the corrupt system of pitt and to carry on unjust unreasonable and liberticide war yes it be perfectly fit and proper that the despotic government they have contribute to restore should make they feel they gratitude if the french since they revolution have not always fight for liberty they have do so invariably for science and wherever they carry they victorious arm abuse be abolish amelioration of all kind follow and the art of life be improve we government since the accession of george iii have never raise its arm except in favor of old abuse to uphold despotism and unfair privilege or to establish commercial monopoly we victory so far from be of beneficial effect to the country wherein we gain they have be they curse we can interfere and be prodigal of money and blood to crush any attempt of the continental nation towards obtain they liberty but when it be necessary to intercede in favor of oppressed patriot then we be tell that we have no right to interfere with the domestic policy of other nation we can send ship to protect and carry off in safety a worthless royal family as at naple in 1799 but we can view with heartless indifference and even complacency the murder commit in spain by the infamous ferdinand and he severity against those to whom he owe he crown all of whom have the strongest daim to we protection as have fight with we in the same cause and contribute to we success the _ platz _ at leipzig be large and here it be that the fair be hold the theater be a elegant building and lie just outside one of the gate of the city innumerable shop of bookseller be here and it be astonishing at how cheap a rate printing in all language be carry forward there be some pleasant promenade in the environs of leipzig but this be not a time of the year to judge of the beauty of the country i go however to view the house occupy by napoleon on the eve of the battle of leipzig a monument be to be erect to the memory of poniatowsky in the spot where he perish i start from leipzig on 7th march at eleven o'clock i be five day en route from leipzig to frankfort tho ' the distance do not exceed forty-five german mile i travel in the diligence but have i know that the arrangement be so uncomfortable i should have prefer go in a _ landkutsche _ which would have make the journey in seven day and afford I a opportunity of stop every night to repose whereas in the diligence tho ' they go _ en poste _ they travel exceedingly slow and it be impossible to persuade the postillion to accelerate he usual pace he be far more careful of he horse than of he passenger this i however excuse but it be of the frequent stoppage and bad arrangement of they that i complain instead of stop at some town for one whole night or two whole night out of the five they stop almost at every town for three four and five hour so that these short stoppage do not give you time enough to go to bed and they be besides generally make in the day time or early in the morning and evening we pass thro ' the follow city and place of eminence viz lutzen the spot where gustavus adolphus be kill be close to the road on the left hand with a plain stone and the initial ga inscribe on it weimar be a very neat city and where i should like much to have staid but i have only time to view the outside of the palace and the _ stadthaus _ erfurt and gotha be both fine look city in gotha i have only time to see the outside of the _ residenz schloss _ or ducal palace which be agreeably situate on a eminence and to remark in the _ neumarkt kirche _ the portrait of duke bernard of saxe weimar and the monument of the prince of that family at erfurt there be the tomb of a count gleichen who be make prisoner in the holy land in the time of the crusade and be release by a mahometan princess on condition of he espouse she the count be already marry in germany and there he have leave he wife but such be he gratitude to the fair musulmane that he marry she with the full consent of he german wife and they all three live happily together fulda where we stop four hour appear a fine city and be situate on a eminence command a noble view of a very fertile and extensive plain the episcopal palace and the church be magnificent and the general appearance of the town be strike the bishopric of fulda be formerly a independent ecclesiastical state but be secularise at the treaty of lunéville and now form part of the territory of hesse-cassel the _ feld-zeichen _ of hesse-cassel be green and red after pass thro ' hanau where we halt three hour which give I a opportunity of view the field of battle there we proceed to frankfort and arrive there at twelve o'clock the 12th of march i put up at the _ swan _ inn in summer time the country about fulda and in general between fulda and frankfort must be very please from the variety of the feature of the ground we live very well and very cheap on the road the price of the diligence from leipzig to frankfort be eleven _ reichsthaler _ after remain three day to repose at frankfort i take my place to mayence and from thence to metz and pari in the diligence from mayence and indeed all the way to pari i find a very amusing society there be two physician and m l -lrb- emaître -rrb- a most entertaining man and of inexhaustible colloquial talent for except when he sleep he never cease to talk he conversation be however always interesting and entertaining for he have figure in the early part of the french revolution and be well know in the political and litterary world as the editor of a famous journal call _ le bonhomme richard _ -lrb- 129 -rrb- metz be a large well build and strongly fortify city verdun thro ' which we pass become quite a english colony during the war from the number of _ detenus _ of that nation who be compel to reside there at epernay we drink a few bottle of champagne and a toast be give by one of the company which meet with general applause it be _ bon voyage _ to the ally who have now finally evacuate france to the great joy of the whole nation except of the town where they be canton where they contribute much towards enrich the shopkeeper and inhabitant i remain in pari six day and then proceed to england -lrb- 129 -rrb- _ le bonhomme richard aux bonnes gen _ be not a famous journal as only
